Majority of Limbs: Tayammum or Washing for the Wounded
Commentary on a matn ruling about tayammum for the wounded based on majority of limbs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of majority (kathrah) to determine whether a wounded person must perform tayammum or wash, and distinguish between the preferred view and the intra-Hanafi dispute on defining majority.

Core Idea
The majority of limbs determines tayammum or washing: the ruling follows the whole.

When a person has wounds on some limbs and water would cause harm, the classical Hanafi jurists faced a practical question: should they wash the healthy parts and wipe the wounds, or skip water altogether and perform tayammum? The ruling turns on a single criterion – majority (al-kathrah). This passage from Kanz al-Daqa’iq explains that if most of the limbs are wounded, tayammum replaces the entire wudu or ghusl. If the healthy parts are more, the healthy parts are washed and the wounds are wiped. The commentator unpacks an intra-Hanafi debate about how to count the majority: by the number of limbs or by the area of each limb. Understanding this precision is essential for correctly applying the rule in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling's condition
The condition is 'majority of limbs wounded' vs. 'majority healthy'. Determine which condition triggers tayammum and which triggers washing + wiping.
For wudu, the unit is each limb (face, hands, head, feet). For ghusl, the unit is the entire body area.
2
Apply the legal maxim
The maxim 'al-akthar lahu hukm al-kull' (the majority takes the ruling of the whole) is applied. Confirm how this maxim yields the ruling.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on majority
Some Hanafi scholars define majority by the number of limbs; others define it by the area of each limb. Note the practical difference: e.g., if one limb has a large wound and three are healthy, the first view gives tayammum, the second gives washing.
The preferred view (in al-Haqa’iq) is majority by number of limbs for wudu.
4
Handle the special case of only hands wounded
If wounds are only on the hands and water harms them, tayammum is permissible even if the rest of the body is healthy, because washing the hands is a pillar.
This is an exception: tayammum for hands while washing other limbs.
5
Note the prohibition of combining tayammum and washing
Tayammum and washing are substitute and original; combining them has no precedent in Shariah. The ruling is for the majority, not a combination.
So if tayammum is done, it covers the whole purification; do not wash afterwards.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ولو أكثره مجروحاً تيمم وبعكسه يغسل أي لو كان أكثر أعضاء الوضوء منه مجروحاً في الحدث الأصغر أو أكثر جميع بدنه في الحدث الأكبر تيمم، وإذا كان الصحيح أكثر من المجروح يغسل لأن للأكثر حكم الكل ويمسح على الجراحة إن لم يضره وإلا فعلى الخرقة. وقد اختلف في حد الكثرة؛ منهم من اعتبر من حيث عدد الأعضاء، ومنهم من اعتبر الكثرة في نفس كل عضو، فلو كان برأسه ووجهه ويديه جراحة والرجل لا جراحة بها يتيمم، سواء كان الأكثر من أعضاء الجراحة جريحاً أو صحيحاً. والآخرون قالوا: إن كان الأكثر من كل عضو من أعضاء الوضوء المذكورة جريحاً فهو الكثير الذي يجوز معه التيمم وإلا فلا كذا في فتح القدير من غير ترجيح وفي الحقائق المختار اعتبار الكثرة من حيث عدد الأعضاء، ولا يخفى أن الخلاف إنما هو الوضوء، وأما في الغسل فالظاهر أن يكون المراد أكثر البدن صحيحاً أو جريحاً الأكثرية من حيث المساحة، فلو استويا لا رواية فيه. واختلف المشايخ منهم من : قال يتيمم ولا يستعمل الماء أصلاً، وقيل يغسل الصحيح ويمسح على الباقي واختار القول الأول في الاختيار وقال أنه أحسن. وفي الخلاصة إنه الأصح. وفي فتح تبعاً للزيلعي أنه الأشبه بالفقه وهو المذكور في النوادر واختار في المحيط الثاني وقال : وهو الأصح. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان وهو الصحيح. ولا يخفى أنه أحوط فكان أولى . وفي القنية والمبتغى بالغين المعجمة : بيده قروح يضره الماء دون سائر جسده يتيمم إذا لم يجد من يغسل وجهه، وقيل يتيمم مطلقاً .اهـ. فهذا يفيد أن قولهم إذا كان الأكثر صحيحاً يغسل الصحيح محمول على ما إذا لم يكن باليدين جراحة كما لا يخفى قوله ( ولا يجمع بينهما) أي لا يجمع بين التيمم والغسل لما فيه من الجمع بين البدل والمبدل ولا نظير له في الشرع فيكون الحكم للأكثر
His statement: 'If most of it is wounded, he performs tayammum; and in the opposite case, he washes.' That is, if most of his wudu limbs are wounded in minor impurity, or most of his entire body in major impurity, he performs tayammum. And if the healthy is more than the wounded, he washes because the majority takes the ruling of the whole, and he wipes over the wound if it does not harm him; otherwise, over the bandage. They differed on the limit of majority: some considered it in terms of number of limbs; some considered majority within each limb. So if his head, face, and hands have wounds and his foot has no wound, he performs tayammum, whether the majority of the wounded limbs are wounded or healthy. And others said: if the majority of each of the mentioned wudu limbs is wounded, then it is the majority for which tayammum is permissible; otherwise not. Thus in Fath al-Qadir without preference. In al-Haqa'iq the chosen view is considering majority by number of limbs. It is not hidden that the disagreement is only in wudu; as for ghusl, the apparent is that what is meant is most of the body, healthy or wounded, the majority is by area. If they are equal, there is no narration. The mashayikh differed: some said he performs tayammum and does not use water at all; some said he washes the healthy and wipes over the remainder. The first was chosen in al-Ikhtiyar and said it is better. In al-Khulasah it is the most correct. In Fath, following al-Zayla'i, it is closest to fiqh and is mentioned in al-Nawadir. In al-Muhit the second was chosen and said it is the most correct. In Fatawa Qadikhan it is the correct. It is not hidden that it is more precautionary and thus more appropriate. In al-Qunyah and al-Mubtagha: 'He has sores on his hand that water harms but the rest of his body is fine; he performs tayammum if he cannot find someone to wash his face; it is said he performs tayammum absolutely.' This indicates that their statement 'if the majority is healthy, he washes the healthy' is restricted to when there is no wound on the hands, as is not hidden. His statement: 'And he does not combine them' means he does not combine tayammum and washing because that would combine the substitute and the original, and there is no parallel to it in the Shariah; thus the ruling is for the majority.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on a matn from Kanz al-Daqa’iq regarding the rule for a wounded person: if the majority of his wudu limbs are wounded, he performs tayammum; if the healthy parts are the majority, he washes (the healthy parts) and wipes over the wounds. The commentator explains that “majority” is determined by the number of limbs, not the area of each limb, according to the preferred view (as in al-Haqa’iq). For ghusl (major impurity), majority is by area of the body. If equal, no clear ruling is transmitted. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: some say if majority is healthy, wash healthy and wipe wounds; others say do tayammum entirely. The chosen view in al-Ikhtiyar and al-Khulasah is to wash healthy parts, but Fatawa Qadikhan considers tayammum more precautionary. The commentator then notes a special case: if the hands have sores, and other limbs are healthy, tayammum is permissible because washing the hands would harm them. Finally, combining tayammum and washing together is prohibited because they are substitute and original, and such combination has no precedent in Shariah.

Key Terms
الكثرة (al-kathrah): Majority; in this passage, the criterion for whether tayammum or washing is performed. For wudu, decided by number of limbs; for ghusl, by area.
الجراحة (al-jarahah): Wound; an injury that may affect the validity of wudu or ghusl if water harms it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person has a small cut on his right hand (one limb) and a large burn on his left leg (one limb), but his face, left hand, right leg, and head are healthy. According to the mufta bihi view, what is the correct ruling?
A) He should perform tayammum because two limbs are wounded.
B) He should wash the healthy limbs (face, left hand, right leg, head) and wipe over the wounds on right hand and left leg.
C) He should only wash the healthy limbs and ignore the wounds.
D) He must combine tayammum and washing.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling for a wounded person turns on the majority of limbs (by number for wudu, by area for ghusl): tayammum if majority wounded; washing and wiping if majority healthy.

Prohibition of Combining Tayammum and Ghusl
Explains prohibition of combining tayammum and ghusl.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that tayammum and ghusl cannot be combined and explain the reasoning based on the substitute-original principle.

Core Idea
A substitute and its original cannot be combined in a single act of worship.

This lesson examines the rule that tayammum and ghusl cannot be performed together. The underlying principle is that combining a substitute (badal) and its original (mubdal) has no parallel in Islamic law. We also contrast this with the case of donkey's leftover water and list other uncombinable pairs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
What exactly is being prohibited? The text says 'they are not combined' – meaning tayammum and ghusl cannot be performed together.
This is the matn statement being commented on.
2
Locate the proof
The proof is rational analogy (qiyas). The reasoning is that combining a substitute and its original has no precedent in shariah; therefore it is invalid.
No explicit Quran or Hadith is cited; the argument is based on the absence of any parallel.
3
Contrast with the donkey's leftover water case
The text contrasts with su'r al-himar, where either tayammum or using that water is sufficient, so they can be combined in case of doubt.
This shows the principle: when the obligation is fulfilled by either, combining is allowed; when one is a substitute, combining is forbidden.
4
Recognize the list of uncombinable pairs
The text then lists many other pairs that cannot be combined, such as menstruation and istihadah, zakat and tithe, etc.
This demonstrates that the principle is widely applied across fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ( ولا يجمع بينهما) أي لا يجمع بين التيمم والغسل لما فيه من الجمع بين البدل والمبدل ولا نظير له في الشرع فيكون الحكم للأكثر
القدير
بالماء الخ» المشي على القول الأول فالأنسب نسخة لا يجب وسنذكر المسألة أيضاً في شروط الصلاة والنسخ هناك مختلفة أيضاً، ففي بعضها الترديد وفي بعضها الجزم بعدم الوجوب، وكان صاحب النهر لم ير عبارة السراج فقال في شروط الصلاة ولو قدر عليه بثمن مثله لم يذكروه وينبغي أن يلزمه قياساً على شراء الماء اهـ . وما بحثه مخالف لما يفيده كلام أخيه قوله : (وإذا كان الصحيح أكثر من المجروح يغسل) أي إذا كان يمكنه غسل الصحيح بدون إصابة الموضع الجريح بالماء، أما إذا كان لا يمكنه غسله إلا بإصابة الماء للجريح على وجه يضره فإنه يتيمم، ففي الخانية وغيرها الجنب إذا كان به جراحات في عامة جسده وهو لا يستطيع غسل الجراحة ويستطيع غسل ما بقي فإنه يتيمم ويصلي لأنه لو غسل غير موضع الجراحة ربما يصل الماء إليها فيضره لا جرم لو أمكنه أن يغسل غير موضع الجراحة ويمسح على الجراحة بالماء إن كان لا يضره المسح أو يعصبها بخرقة ويمسح على الخرقة فعل، وإن كان أكثر أعضائه صحيحاً بأن كانت الجراحة على رأسه وسائر جسده صحيح فإنه يدع الرأس ويغسل سائر الأعضاء .اهـ. كذا في شرح المنية لابن أمير حاج . فأفاد أن الجراحة لو كانت بظهره مثلاً بحيث لو غسل ما فوقها أصابها الماء لا يلزمه غسله، وأفاد أيضاً أنه لو كان لا يمكنه مسح الجراحة إلا إذا عصبها لزمه تعصيبها ومسح العصابة قوله : أما في الغسل الخ) نقله العلامة
٢٨٦
كتاب الطهارة - باب التيمم
،
بخلاف الجمع بين التيمم وسؤر الحمار لأن الفرض يتأدى بأحدهما لا بهما فجمعنا بينهما لمكان الشك، وكما لا جمع بين التيمم والغسل لا جمع بين الحيض والاستحاضة، ولا بين الحيض والنفاس، ولا بين الاستحاضة ،والنفاس ولا بين الحيض والحبل ولا بين الزكاة والعشر، ولا بين العشر والخراج ولا بين الفطرة والزكاة ولا بين الفدية والصوم ولا بين القطع والضمان، ولا بين الجلد والنفي ولا بين القصاص والكفارة، ولا بين الحد والمهر ولا بین المتعة والمهر وغيرها من المسائل الآتية في مواضعها إن شاء الله تعالى، وما وقع في خزانة الفقه لأبي الليث أن عشرة لا تجتمع مع عشرة فليس للحصر كما لا يخفى.
His statement (and they are not combined) means tayammum and ghusl are not combined, because it involves combining a substitute and the original, and there is no parallel for this in Islamic law, so the ruling is for the majority. ... Unlike the combination of tayammum and the leftover water of a donkey, because the obligation is fulfilled by either one, not both, so we combine them due to doubt. And just as there is no combination between tayammum and ghusl, there is no combination between menstruation and istihadah, nor between menstruation and postpartum bleeding, nor between istihadah and postpartum, nor between menstruation and pregnancy, nor between zakat and tithe, nor between tithe and kharaj, nor between fitrah and zakat, nor between fidyah and fasting, nor between amputation and compensation, nor between flogging and exile, nor between qisas and kaffarah, nor between hadd and mahr, nor between mut'ah and mahr, and other issues that will come in their places, God willing. And what is found in Khizanat al-Fiqh of Abu al-Layth that ten does not combine with ten is not exhaustive, as is not hidden.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn phrase 'and they are not combined', explaining the legal principle that tayammum (the substitute) and ghusl (the original ablution) cannot be performed together. The reason is that combining a substitute (badal) with the original (mubdal) has no precedent in shariah. The commentator then draws a contrast with the case of tayammum and donkey's saliva (su'r al-himar), where either is sufficient, so they can be combined in case of doubt. He then lists numerous pairs of rulings that cannot be combined, such as menstruation and istihadah, zakat and tithe, etc., to illustrate that this principle is widely applied. The long digression in the middle (from 'قوله : (وإذا كان الصحيح أكثر)' to 'قوله : أما في الغسل الخ') is an extended clarification of the rule about washing the healthy parts when the majority is healthy, with emphasis on avoiding harm to wounds.

Key Terms
البدل (al-badal): A substitute; tayammum is a substitute for wudu or ghusl.
المبدل (al-mubdal): The original act for which the substitute is made, e.g., ghusl with water.
سؤر الحمار (su'r al-himar): The leftover water after a donkey drinks; considered pure but disliked in Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why can tayammum and ghusl not be combined according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because water is always available
B) Because combining a substitute and the original has no parallel in shariah
C) Because tayammum is not valid for janabah
D) Because ghusl is always wajib

Key Takeaway
Tayammum and ghusl cannot be combined because a substitute and its original cannot coexist in a single act.

The Ruling for a Wounded Person in Tayammum
Explains the ruling for a wounded person regarding washing and tayammum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling for a wounded person regarding washing healthy parts and performing tayammum on the wound.

Core Idea
If the majority of the body is healthy, those parts must be washed; if washing would harm the wound, tayammum is performed.

This lesson covers the scenario where a person has wounds on some parts of the body. The Hanafi school provides detailed guidance on when to wash healthy parts and when to resort to tayammum for the wounded areas. The key is to avoid harm while ensuring purification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The text discusses a person who has wounds on part of their body but the majority is healthy.
The ruling depends on whether the majority is healthy or wounded.
2
State the general rule
If the majority of the body is healthy, the healthy parts must be washed with water. The wound itself is not washed if water would harm it.
The text says 'if the healthy is more than the wounded, he washes the healthy parts'.
3
Explain the exception
If washing the healthy parts would inevitably cause water to reach the wound and harm it, then tayammum is performed instead of washing.
This is to prevent harm.
4
Detail the method for wounds
If possible, the wound should be wiped with water (if not harmful) or a wet bandage should be wiped. If neither is possible, tayammum is sufficient.
The text describes options: wipe the wound, or bandage and wipe over it.
5
Apply to specific cases
Example: if the wound is on the head and the rest of the body is healthy, one leaves the head and washes the rest.
This demonstrates the application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ( ولا يجمع بينهما) أي لا يجمع بين التيمم والغسل لما فيه من الجمع بين البدل والمبدل ولا نظير له في الشرع فيكون الحكم للأكثر
القدير

٢٨٦

،

His statement (and they are not combined) means tayammum and ghusl are not combined, because it involves combining a substitute and the original, and there is no parallel for this in Islamic law, so the ruling is for the majority. ... Unlike the combination of tayammum and the leftover water of a donkey, because the obligation is fulfilled by either one, not both, so we combine them due to doubt. The reason is that combining a substitute (badal) with the original (mubdal) has no precedent in shariah. Key Terms
الجرح (al-jurh): A wound or injury on the body.
التيمم (al-tayammum): Dry ablution with dust as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, if a person has a wound on his head and the rest of the body is healthy, what should he do for ghusl?
A) Wash the entire body including the head with water
B) Leave the head and wash the rest of the body
C) Perform tayammum for the entire body
D) Wash the head only with water

Key Takeaway
When the majority of the body is healthy, wash the healthy parts; for the wounded part, use tayammum or a wet bandage to avoid harm.

Rulings on Tayammum and Subsequent Water
Subsidiary rulings on tayammum and subsequent water availability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings on tayammum and subsequent water availability, specifically determining when to perform wudu, tayammum, or remove khuff.

Core Idea
Tayammum is invalidated by finding water or by hadath; each scenario requires re-evaluation of purification method.

The Hanafi school provides detailed scenarios for a person who performed tayammum and later encounters water. This lesson unpacks a passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq that illustrates how the availability of water and the state of hadath interact with the rulings of wudu, tayammum, and wiping over khuff. Understanding these subsidiary rulings (furu') is essential for correctly applying the rules of purification in fluctuating conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial act
Recognize that the person performed tayammum for janabah and prayed. This establishes a valid purification for that prayer.
Tayammum is a temporary purification valid only while water is absent.
2
Note the change in status
After the prayer, two things happen: minor hadath occurs and water becomes available. Assess which purification method is now required.
Hadath invalidates tayammum for future acts; water availability overrides tayammum.
3
Apply the ruling for wudu
Since water is available for wudu and hadath is present, the person must make wudu for the next prayer. Tayammum is no longer sufficient.
The hadath does not require ghusl; wudu suffices for minor impurity.
4
Consider the scenario with khuff
After performing wudu, he wears leather socks (khuff). Then he passes by water but does not perform ghusl, and later becomes without water. Now, for the next prayer, he has water for wudu but not for ghusl. He must perform tayammum, not wudu, because the obligation of ghusl remains? Actually, the text says he performs tayammum. This is because the original janabah still requires ghusl, and since he cannot perform ghusl, tayammum substitutes for janabah. Wudu alone does not remove janabah.
Key distinction: hadath vs janabah. The presence of water for wudu does not remove the need for ghusl.
5
Handling later hadath after tayammum
If after tayammum, another prayer time arrives and he is already in a state of minor hadath, and he has water for wudu, then he must make wudu and remove his khuff. This is because the tayammum was for janabah, not for hadath. Hadath requires wudu, and since water is available, wudu is obligatory.
Removing khuff is necessary because wudu requires washing the feet, and wiping over khuff is only valid if the khuff was put on after wudu with water.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فروع رجل تيمم للجنابة وصلى ثم أحدث ومعه من الماء قدر ما يتوضأ به فإنه يتوضأ به لصلاة أخرى، فإن توضأ به ولبس خفيه ثم مرّ بالماء ولم يغتسل حتى صار عادماً الماء ثم حضرت الصلاة ومعه من الماء قدر ما يتوضأ به فإنه يتيمم ولا يتوضأ، فإن تيمم ثم حضرت الصلاة الأخرى وقد سبقه الحدث فإنه يتوضأ به وينزع خفيه، وإن لم يكن مرّ بماء قبل ذلك على خفيه.
Subsidiary issues: A man performs tayammum for janabah and prays, then experiences minor impurity, and has with him water enough for wudu. Then he makes wudu with it for another prayer. If he makes wudu with it and wears his leather socks (khuffayn), then passes by water and does not perform ghusl until he becomes without water, then the prayer time comes and he has with him water enough for wudu, then he performs tayammum and does not make wudu. If he performs tayammum, then another prayer time comes and he is already in a state of minor impurity (hadath), then he makes wudu with it and removes his leather socks. If he had not passed by water before that, then his ruling is upon his leather socks.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage presents a series of subsidiary rulings (furu') related to a person who has performed tayammum for janabah (major impurity) and then encounters water. The rulings are conditional: If after tayammum and prayer he has minor impurity and has water for wudu, he uses it for the next prayer. If he then wears leather socks and later lacks water, he performs tayammum again. If he later has water for wudu but has minor impurity, he must make wudu and remove his leather socks. These rules balance the availability of water with the validity of tayammum and the ruling of wiping over leather socks.

Key Terms
الخف (al-khuff): Leather sock that can be wiped over during wudu for a limited period.
الحدث (al-hadath): State of ritual impurity that requires wudu (minor) or ghusl (major).
الجنابة (al-janabah): Major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person performs tayammum for janabah, prays, then has minor impurity and has water for wudu, what must he do for the next prayer?
A) Perform tayammum again
B) Make wudu
C) Make ghusl
D) Pray without purification

Key Takeaway
The availability of water and the type of impurity determine whether wudu, tayammum, or ghusl is required, and conditions like passing water affect the ruling on leather socks.

When Purification is Impossible: The Faqid al-Ṭahūrayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on praying without purification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on the faqid al-tahurayn, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
When neither water nor earth is available, Abu Hanifa says wait; Abu Yusuf says pray with gestures.

Imagine being trapped in a filthy place with no access to water or pure earth. Can you still pray? The Hanafi school has a nuanced dispute on this precise scenario. In this lesson, we examine the ruling for the faqid al-tahurayn (one lacking both purifiers) as presented in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, and explore the reasoning behind the differing opinions of the founding imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling's subject
First, understand the exact situation: a person confined in a najis place, with no pure water, pure earth, or clean spot. The act under discussion is the obligation of prayer (salat).
The scenario is 'in the city' (fi al-misr), implying it is not a travel situation.
2
State the position of Abu Hanifa
According to Abu Hanifa and one riwaya from Muhammad, the person should not pray until finding a purifier. Prayer without purification is invalid.
This is the zahir al-riwayah position.
3
State the position of Abu Yusuf
Abu Yusuf holds that the person should pray with gestures (ima), i.e., nodding for ruku and sujud, to resemble the worshippers and avoid missing prayer entirely.
Some refine this: if the ground is dry, actual bowing and prostration are possible; if wet, only gestures.
4
Analyze the basis of each opinion
Abu Hanifa emphasizes the condition (shart) of purification for the validity of prayer. Abu Yusuf prioritizes the obligation of prayer itself, considering gesture as a substitute when purification is impossible.
The text does not record a direct rebuttal; it simply presents the difference.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa's view, the person must delay prayer; under Abu Yusuf's, he prays immediately with gestures, though such prayer is considered incomplete.
Later Hanafi fatwa may lean toward Abu Yusuf for necessity, but the text gives no tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفاقد الطهورين في المصر بأن حبس في مكان نجس ولم يجد مكاناً طاهراً ولا ماء طاهراً ولا تراباً طاهراً لا يصلي حتى يجد أحدهما. وقال أبو يوسف : يصلي بالإيماء تشبهاً بالمصليين قال بعضهم: إنما يصلي بالإيماء على قوله إذا لم يكن الموضع يابساً، أما إذا كان يابساً يصلي بركوع وسجود، ومحمد في بعض الروايات مع أبي حنيفة.
And one who lacks both purifiers in the city, such that he is confined in a filthy place and cannot find a pure place, nor pure water, nor pure earth, does not pray until he finds one of them. Abu Yusuf said: he prays with gesture (ima) to resemble the worshippers. Some said: he prays with gesture according to his view if the place is not dry; if it is dry, he prays with bowing and prostration. Muhammad in some narrations agrees with Abu Hanifa.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage discusses the case of a person who is trapped in a filthy place and has access to no pure water or pure earth (the two purifiers). The Hanafi school has a dispute: Abu Hanifa and, in some narrations, Muhammad say that such a person should not pray at all until he finds a purifier, because valid prayer requires something to purify with. Abu Yusuf, however, says he should pray by gesture (ima), i.e., nodding for bowing and prostration, to avoid missing the prayer entirely. Some scholars refine Abu Yusuf's view: if the ground is dry, he can do actual bowing and prostration on it without purification; if it is wet (najis), he uses gesture. The commentary does not give a definitive tarjih here.

Key Terms
فاقد الطهورين (faqid al-tahurayn): One who lacks both water and earth (the two purifiers) for purification.
الإيماء (al-ima'): Gestures used in prayer instead of actual bowing and prostration, for those who are unable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what must a person do if he is trapped in a filthy place with no pure water or earth?
A) Pray with gestures (ima)
B) Not pray until he finds a purifier
C) Perform tayammum with the filthy earth
D) Pray normally without purification

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, when both water and pure earth are unavailable, Abu Hanifa says no prayer, Abu Yusuf says pray with gestures; the practical consequence is either missing prayer or performing it with ima.

Ijma' on Prohibiting Prayer During Movement and Its Exception
Consensus rulings on prohibition of prayer during movement or combat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the consensus ruling on praying while walking, swimming, or fighting, and identify the condition under which tayammum becomes permissible.

Core Idea
Consensus forbids prayer during motion; only pure earth enables valid prayer.

This passage from al-Khulasa presents a matter of consensus (ijma) among the scholars that engaging in the obligatory prayer while walking, swimming, or actively fighting is impermissible. The reason is that proper prayer requires stillness and facing the qibla. However, an exception is made if one can access pure earth to perform tayammum, allowing the prayer to be offered properly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
The passage states a consensus that the walker, swimmer, and sword-fighter do not pray while in motion. The basis is ijma, which is a primary source of law.
2
Recognize the exception
If the person can scratch the ground or wall to obtain pure earth, he can perform tayammum and pray properly, by consensus.
3
Understand the condition for the exception
The exception applies only when it is possible to obtain pure earth. If not, the original prohibition remains.
The text says 'wa hadha idha lam yumkinhu an yanqur al-ard... fa in amkanahu yastakhriju al-turab al-tahir wa yusalli'.
4
Apply the ruling to real scenarios
Consider a traveler who cannot stop walking or someone thrown into water; they cannot pray while moving unless they can reach pure earth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأجمعوا أن الماشي لا يصلي وهو يمشي، والسابح لا يصلي وهو يسبح، ولا السائف وهو يضرب بالسيف وإن خاف فوت الوقت. وهذا إذا لم يمكنه أن ينقر الأرض أو الحائط بشيء، فإن أمكنه يستخرج التراب الطاهر ويصلي بالإجماع كذا في الخلاصة.
And they (the scholars) agreed that the walker does not pray while walking, nor the swimmer while swimming, nor the sword-fighter while striking with the sword, even if he fears missing the time. This is the case if he cannot scratch the ground or the wall with something; if he can, he extracts pure earth and prays, by consensus. Thus in al-Khulasa.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage states a matter of consensus (ijma) that it is not permissible to pray while walking, swimming, or engaged in combat with a sword, even if one fears the prayer time will end. The reason is that proper prayer requires stillness and facing the qibla. However, an exception is made if one can access pure earth by scratching the ground or wall with something; then he can perform tayammum and pray properly. This is also by consensus.

Key Terms
الإجماع (al-ijma'): Consensus of the mujtahids on a ruling; considered a primary source of law.
السائف (al-sa'if): One who fights with a sword, striking blows.

Head Pain Exempting from Wiping (Masah) in Wudu
Unique ruling exempting masah due to head pain

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rare Hanafi ruling that head pain drops the obligation of masah and identify the sources and authority behind it.

Core Idea
Head pain can lift the wajib of masah — a rare necessity-based exception in purification.

This lesson examines an exceptional ruling from the Hanafi school: the obligation to wipe the head in wudu can be dropped due to head pain. This ruling is not widely found in standard texts, coming from al-Jallabi's rare transmission and confirmed by later authorities like Siraj al-Din Qari' al-Hidayah. Understanding such exceptions enriches your grasp of how necessity can modify obligations in fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Recall the usual ruling for masah
In standard Hanafi wudu, wiping the head (masah) is a wajib (obligatory) act. This is the baseline.
2
Identify the exception
Al-Jallabi reports a rare ruling: if a person has head pain, the obligation of masah is dropped for him. The word 'yasqut' (falls) indicates complete removal of the obligation.
The pain is unspecified — any genuine head pain suffices.
3
Trace the transmission chain
The ruling is from al-Jallabi's book on prayer, not found in the six core books (Zahir al-Riwayah). It is a gharib (rare) transmission.
4
Assess the authority
Siraj al-Din Qari' al-Hidayah, a major Hanafi authority, gave a fatwa based on this transmission, lending it weight. The commentator Ibn Amir Haj mentions it to resolve previous doubts.
5
Apply the lesson
This exemplifies a necessity-based exception: when an obligatory act causes harm, it may be lifted. However, because the ruling is rare, it should be applied cautiously.
Not all Hanafi books include this; it is considered gharib.

Source Text

The Principle of Non-Combination (La Jam') in Acts of Worship
Enumerating cases where two acts do not combine

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle of non-combination (la jam') and apply it to identify when two legal acts cannot be performed simultaneously.

Core Idea
When each act alone suffices for the obligation, combining them is invalid – the act is performed by one, not both.

This passage from Bahr al-Raiq lays out a foundational Hanafi rule: in acts of worship, if two different legal acts can each fulfill the same obligation, they are not combined. The only exception is when doubt (shakk) exists, as with tayammum and the leftover of a donkey. This principle applies across purification, zakat, criminal law, and more, illustrating the internal consistency of Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exception
Note that the passage begins by contrasting with a case where combination IS allowed: tayammum and su'r al-himar. Understand the reason: because the obligatory act is performed by one of them, not both, but we combine due to doubt.
This exception is based on uncertainty about which one actually fulfills the obligation.
2
State the general principle
The core rule: two acts that each singly suffice for the same obligation cannot be combined. The reasoning is that the obligation is discharged by one of them – combining would imply doubt about which is effective.
This rule applies when both acts are valid alternatives for the same duty.
3
Enumerate the listed pairs
The passage lists thirteen pairs (including the exception): (1) tayammum & leftover water of donkey (exception), (2) tayammum & ghusl, (3) hayd & istihadah, (4) hayd & nifas, (5) istihadah & nifas, (6) hayd & pregnancy, (7) zakat & 'ushr, (8) 'ushr & kharaj, (9) fitrah & zakat, (10) fidyah & fasting, (11) amputation & guarantee, (12) flogging & exile, (13) qisas & kaffarah, (14) hadd & mahr, (15) mut'ah & mahr. Recognize each as a situation where two rulings could apply but only one should.
The list is illustrative, not exhaustive.
4
Understand the limited scope
The author notes that Abu al-Layth's statement that 'ten do not combine with ten' is not a complete enumeration. This reminds us that the principle is broad and other cases exist beyond those mentioned.
When applying the principle, always consider the underlying reasoning rather than a fixed list.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بخلاف الجمع بين التيمم وسؤر الحمار لأن الفرض يتأدى بأحدهما لا بهما فجمعنا بينهما لمكان الشك، وكما لا جمع بين التيمم والغسل لا جمع بين الحيض والاستحاضة، ولا بين الحيض والنفاس، ولا بين الاستحاضة والنفاس ولا بين الحيض والحبل ولا بين الزكاة والعشر، ولا بين العشر والخراج ولا بين الفطرة والزكاة ولا بين الفدية والصوم ولا بين القطع والضمان، ولا بين الجلد والنفي ولا بين القصاص والكفارة، ولا بين الحد والمهر ولا بين المتعة والمهر وغيرها من المسائل الآتية في مواضعها إن شاء الله تعالى، وما وقع في خزانة الفقه لأبي الليث أن عشرة لا تجتمع مع عشرة فليس للحصر كما لا يخفى.
Unlike the combination between tayammum and the leftover of a donkey, because the obligatory act is performed by one of them, not by both, so we combine them due to doubt. And just as there is no combination between tayammum and ghusl, there is no combination between hayd and istihadah, nor between hayd and nifas, nor between istihadah and nifas, nor between hayd and pregnancy, nor between zakat and 'ushr, nor between 'ushr and kharaj, nor between fitrah and zakat, nor between fidyah and fasting, nor between amputation and guarantee, nor between flogging and exile, nor between qisas and kaffarah, nor between hadd and mahr, nor between mut'ah and mahr, and other cases that will come in their places, God willing. And what is in Khizanat al-Fiqh of Abu al-Layth that ten do not combine with ten, it is not for enumeration, as is not hidden.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage states a Hanafi legal principle: certain acts do not combine when each alone suffices to discharge the obligation. The reason is that mixing them would imply uncertainty about which fulfills the duty. The text then enumerates various pairs that cannot be combined, such as tayammum and ghusl (since tayammum replaces ghusl), hayd and istihadah (differing rulings), etc. These are applications of the principle that when two rulings conflict, they cannot both apply simultaneously. The author notes that Abu al-Layth's statement that 'ten do not combine with ten' is not exhaustive.

Key Terms
الجمع (al-jam'): Combining two different legal acts to fulfill a single obligation
سؤر الحمار (su'r al-himar): The leftover water after a donkey drinks
الفرض (al-fard): An obligatory act that must be performed
شك (shakk): Doubt, uncertainty that triggers the exception for combining

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is there no combination between tayammum and ghusl?
A) Because tayammum is not valid when water exists
B) Because the obligation is performed by one of them, not both
C) Because both are required to be pure
D) Because ghusl cannot be replaced by tayammum

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle of la jam' prohibits combining two acts that each singly suffice for the same obligation, with the exception of cases involving doubt (shakk).

Rulings on Tayammum for Janabah and Subsequent Water Access
Ruling statement with four subsidiary cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wudu after tayammum for janabah, apply the rules regarding khuffs, and distinguish between when wudu or tayammum is required based on water availability and hadath status.

Core Idea
Tayammum does not remove janabah; water found later obligates wudu for any subsequent prayer.

This passage presents a set of subsidiary rulings (furu‘) that test your understanding of how tayammum interacts with later access to water. The key principle is that tayammum for janabah only permits prayer temporarily; it does not lift the state of major impurity. Therefore, any new prayer that falls after water becomes available requires purification with water, subject to specific conditions about hadath (minor impurity) and the wearing of khuffs. The rulings here refine the general rule by addressing scenarios with limited water and the presence of minor events.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first scenario
A man performs tayammum for janabah, prays, then has a minor event (breaks wudu) and finds water sufficient for wudu. What must he do for the next prayer? The text says he performs wudu, not ghusl.
This establishes the baseline: tayammum does not remove janabah, so when water is available, wudu suffices for a new prayer.
2
Add the khuff and water-passing scenario
He performs wudu, wears khuffs, then passes by water but does not perform ghusl. Later he runs out of water. At prayer time, he has only enough water for wudu. What does he do? The text says he performs tayammum, not wudu, because he is still in janabah and the water is less than required for ghusl.
Key point: when water is insufficient for ghusl, tayammum is performed despite having water for wudu.
3
Examine the event-preceded scenario
After that tayammum, a new prayer time comes, but he had a minor event (hadath) before that. He now has water for wudu. The text says he performs wudu with it and removes his khuffs (if he had not previously passed water over them).
The minor event breaks the tayammum? Actually, tayammum remains valid until water is found. The ruling shows that if water is available, wudu is required for the new prayer.
4
Understand the khuff condition
The removal of khuffs is conditioned on whether he had passed water over them (i.e., performed masah while wearing them after wudu). If he had not, he must remove them for wudu; if he had, then his wudu would be valid with wiping.
This connects to the rules of wiping over khuffs: masah is only valid if you are in a state of wudu when you first wear them after wudu.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فروع رجل تيمم للجنابة وصلى ثم أحدث ومعه من الماء قدر ما يتوضأ به فإنه يتوضأ به لصلاة أخرى، فإن توضأ به ولبس خفيه ثم مرّ بالماء ولم يغتسل حتى صار عادماً الماء ثم حضرت الصلاة ومعه من الماء قدر ما يتوضأ به فإنه يتيمم ولا يتوضأ، فإن تيمم ثم حضرت الصلاة الأخرى وقد سبقه الحدث فإنه يتوضأ به وينزع خفيه، وإن لم يكن مرّ بماء قبل ذلك على خفيه.
Branches: A man performed tayammum for janabah and prayed, then had an event (minor impurity) and he has with him water sufficient for wudu. He performs wudu with it for another prayer. If he performs wudu with it and wears his khuffs, then passes by water but does not perform ghusl until he becomes without water, then the prayer time comes and he has with him water sufficient for wudu: he performs tayammum and does not perform wudu. If he performs tayammum then another prayer time comes and the event preceded him, he performs wudu with it and removes his khuffs, if he had not passed by water before that upon his khuffs.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage presents subsidiary rulings (furu') on the interaction between tayammum and subsequent availability of water. The key is that tayammum for janabah does not remove the major impurity; it only permits prayer temporarily. When water becomes available, wudu is required for the next prayer. However, if someone has water but is unable to use it due to being without it at the time of prayer, tayammum is valid. The ruling about khuffs depends on whether he had passed water over them (meaning he had wiped them while wearing them after wudu). If he had not, he must remove them for wudu.

Key Terms
الجنابة (al-janabah): State of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl
الخف (al-khuff): Leather sock worn over the foot, allowing wiping over it in wudu

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because he is in a state of minor impurity and tayammum is easier
B) Because he is still in janabah and water is insufficient for ghusl, so tayammum is his purification
C) Because he had already performed tayammum earlier, so he can repeat it
D) Because water for wudu is not sufficient to remove impurity

Key Takeaway
When water is found after tayammum for janabah, wudu suffices for the next prayer if water is enough for wudu; if water is insufficient for ghusl and the person remains in janabah, tayammum is performed.

Prayer Without Purification: The Faqid al-Tahurayn Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on faqid al-tahurayn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the faqid al-tahurayn case and apply the tarjih to determine the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Without water or earth, prayer is suspended until purification is possible.

This lesson explores a unique intra-Hanafi disagreement: what should a person do if they are trapped in a polluted place with no access to water or pure earth? The majority view of Abu Hanifah and Muhammad holds that prayer is invalid without any purification, while Abu Yusuf permits a gesture prayer to maintain the appearance of worship. Understanding this dispute sharpens your grasp of the priority of purification conditions in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario and the Core Ruling
Read the passage to understand the exact case: a person confined in a city in an impure place, lacking water and earth. Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifah and Muhammad according to the text.
The text says 'la yusalli hatta yajida ahadahuma' (he does not pray until he finds one of them).
2
Analyze Abu Yusuf's Exception
Find Abu Yusuf's position: he allows prayer with gestures (ima') to imitate those who pray. Note the refinement about dry vs. wet ground.
Some say ima' only if the place is wet; if dry, he prays normally because the ground itself is not impure.
3
Evaluate the Tarjih and Consensus Narrations
The passage ends by citing al-Khulasa, stating that if earth can be extracted from a wall, prayer is valid by consensus. This implies the mufta bihi is the stricter view of Abu Hanifah.
The phrase 'kadha fi al-khulasah' indicates the relied-upon view.
4
Apply to Parallel Cases
The passage lists other situations: walker, swimmer, swordsman – none may pray while performing those acts, even if the time is about to end. This reinforces that the condition of purification takes precedence.
These cases are mentioned to show the consistency of the school's principle.
5
Derive the Practical Consequence (Thamarah)
In practice, a person stuck in such a situation must wait until purification is possible. Following Abu Yusuf would allow gesture prayer only if no dry ground is available, but the mufta bihi is to wait.
The difference impacts real-life scenarios like being trapped in a filthy room.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفاقد الطهورين في المصر بأن حبس في مكان نجس ولم يجد مكاناً طاهراً ولا ماء طاهراً ولا تراباً طاهراً لا يصلي حتى يجد أحدهما. وقال أبو يوسف : يصلي بالإيماء تشبهاً بالمصلين قال بعضهم: إنما يصلي بالإيماء على قوله إذا لم يكن الموضع يابساً، أما إذا كان يابساً يصلي بركوع وسجود، ومحمد في بعض الروايات مع أبي حنيفة. وأجمعوا أن الماشي لا يصلي وهو يمشي، والسابح لا يصلي وهو يسبح، ولا السائف وهو يضرب بالسيف وإن خاف فوت الوقت. وهذا إذا لم يمكنه أن ينقر الأرض أو الحائط بشيء، فإن أمكنه يستخرج التراب الطاهر ويصلي بالإجماع كذا في الخلاصة.
And the one who lacks both purifiers in the city, such as being imprisoned in a polluted place and cannot find a pure place, nor pure water, nor pure earth: he does not pray until he finds one of them. Abu Yusuf said: He prays with gestures (ima') imitating those who pray. Some said: He only prays with gestures according to him if the place is not dry; if it is dry, he prays with bowing and prostration. Muhammad, in some narrations, is with Abu Hanifah. And they all agree that the walker does not pray while walking, nor the swimmer while swimming, nor the one striking with the sword even if he fears missing the time. This is if he cannot strike the ground or wall with something; if he can, he extracts pure earth and prays by consensus, as in al-Khulasa.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage addresses a special case: a person in a city who is confined in a place that is impure and has access to no pure water or earth. Abu Hanifah and Muhammad (in one narration) hold that he must wait until he can find one of the purifiers; he does not pray at all. Abu Yusuf argues that he should pray with gestures (like nodding for bowing and prostration) to imitate the congregation, to maintain the appearance of prayer. Some commentators specify that gesture prayer applies only if the ground is wet (i.e., dirty); if dry, he can bow and prostrate normally because the ground itself is not impure. The rest of the passage confirms that walking, swimming, or fighting do not permit prayer even if the time is about to be missed. However, if he can extract pure earth from a wall or floor, he must do so and pray with full movements (consensus).

Key Terms
فاقد الطهورين (faqid al-tahurayn): A person without access to both water (for wudu/ghusl) and pure earth (for tayammum)
الإيماء (al-ima'): Gesture prayer, performed by nodding for bowing and prostration

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position in the Hanafi school, what does the faqid al-tahurayn in a city do?
A) He prays with gestures (ima')
B) He prays normally on the impure ground
C) He does not pray until he finds a purifier
D) He performs tayammum on the wall and prays

Key Takeaway
A person without water or earth must wait until purification is possible; the condition of purity overrides the desire to pray on time.

Head Wound Prevents Wiping: Ruling and Its Source
A rare ruling on dropping head wipe obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a person with a head injury that makes wiping harmful, distinguish it from tayammum, and identify the source (nawadir) of this ruling.

Core Idea
If a head wound makes wiping harmful, the obligation drops entirely — no tayammum needed.

This lesson introduces a rare but important Hanafi ruling: when a person has a head injury that prevents wiping (in wudu or ghusl), the obligation to wipe the head is dropped. This is not a case for tayammum, because tayammum substitutes for washing (ghusl), not for wiping (mash). We will explore the source of this ruling and its reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
The text states that if a person has a head injury that makes wiping harmful, the obligation of wiping (in wudu or ghusl) is dropped entirely.
The Arabic phrase 'yasqutu fard al-mash' means the obligation falls away.
2
Distinguish from Tayammum
The text explicitly says tayammum is not done because the head is normally wiped, not washed; tayammum substitutes for washing, not for wiping.
This is a critical distinction: the head wipe is not a washed limb, so tayammum does not replace it.
3
Understand the Reasoning
The person is considered legally to not have that limb (the head) for the purpose of wiping, similar to a missing limb. Therefore, the function (wiping) drops.
This is a legal fiction (hukman) to excuse the act.
4
Note the Authority
This is a rare transmission (nawadir) from al-Jullabi's Book of Prayer, later upheld by Siraj al-Din Qari' al-Hidayah. It is not from the six core books of Zahir al-Riwayah.
Later Hanafi scholars gave fatwa on it, making it mufta bihi in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر الجلابي في كتاب الصلاة له أن من به وجع في رأسه معه مسحه يسقط فرض المسح في حقه .اهـ. وهذه مسألة مهمة أحببت ذكرها لغرابتها وعدم وجودها في غالب الكتب، وقد أفتى بها الشيخ سراج الدين قارئ الهداية أستاذ المحقق كمال الدين بن الهمام و به اندفع ما كان قد توهم قبل الوقوف على هذا النقل وفي الخلاصة يستطيع نوح أفندي عن حواشي العلامة قاسم على شرح المجمع . قوله : (وبه اندفع ما كان قد توهم قبل أنه يتيمم لعجزه عن استعمال الماء وليس بعد النقل إلا الرجوع إليه، ولعل الوجه فيه أن يجعل عادماً لذلك العضو حكماً فتسقط وظيفته كما في المعدوم حقيقة بخلاف ما إذا كان ببعض الأعضاء المغسولة جراحة فإنه يغسل الصحيح ويمسح على الجريح لأن المسح عليه كالغسل لما تحته ولأن التيمم مسح فلا يكون بدلاً عن مسح وإنما هو بدل عن غسل والرأس ممسوح ولهذا لم يكن التيمم في الرأس، وسيأتي في آخر باب المسح على الخفين لهذا زيادة تحقيق إن شاء الله تعالى.
And al-Jullabi mentioned in his Book of Prayer that if a person has a pain in his head that harms his wiping, the obligation of wiping drops from him. End. This is an important issue, I liked to mention it due to its rarity and its absence in most books. Sheikh Siraj al-Din Qari' al-Hidayah, teacher of the researcher Kamal al-Din ibn al-Humam, gave a fatwa on it, and with it was refuted what had been imagined before finding this transmission: that he performs tayammum due to his inability to use water. There is no recourse except after transmission. Perhaps the reasoning is that he is considered to be without that limb legally, so its function drops, just as in the case of a truly missing limb, unlike when there is a wound on some of the limbs that are washed: he washes the healthy part and wipes over the wound, because wiping over it is like washing under it, and because tayammum is wiping, so it cannot be a substitute for wiping; rather it is a substitute for washing, and the head is wiped, so tayammum is not done on the head. More verification will come at the end of the chapter on wiping over khuffs, God willing.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage presents a rare ruling: if a person has a head injury such that wiping (in wudu or ghusl) causes harm, the obligation of wiping the head is entirely dropped. This is not tayammum, because the head is normally wiped, not washed; tayammum substitutes for washing, not for wiping. Therefore, the person simply omits the head wipe. The text cites al-Jullabi and fatwa from Sheikh Siraj al-Din Qari' al-Hidayah. The reasoning: the head is legally considered non-existent regarding the function of wiping, similar to a missing limb. This differs from a wound on a washed limb, where one washes the healthy part and wipes the wound.

Key Terms
فرض المسح (fard al-mash): The obligatory act of wiping the head in wudu
التيمم (al-tayammum): Dry purification with clean earth as a substitute for water

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for a person whose head wound makes wiping harmful?
A) He performs tayammum
B) He wipes over a bandage
C) The obligation of wiping drops
D) He performs ghusl instead

Key Takeaway
A head injury that makes wiping harmful completely removes the obligation of head wipe in wudu/ghusl, without requiring tayammum.

Definition and Duration of Wiping over Khuffs
Definition of mash and khuff, and duration for resident and traveler

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mash and khuff in Hanafi fiqh, state the prescribed duration for the resident and traveler, and explain the legal reasoning for the precedence of mash over khuffs.

Core Idea
Mash over khuffs is a fixed-duration concession: one day for the resident, three for the traveler.

This lesson opens the chapter on wiping over khuffs (mash ala al-khuffayn). The author explains why this chapter follows tayammum, then defines the key terms and their durations. Understanding this definition is essential for correctly applying this concession in daily wudu practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its category
Recognize that mash over khuffs is a form of purification (taharah) by wiping, not washing. It is a limited concession (rukhsah muqaddarah).
2
Understand the definition of mash
Linguistically: passing the hand over something. Terminologically: a limited concession with a fixed time – one day and night for a resident, three days and nights for a traveler.
3
Understand the definition of khuff
In Shari'ah: leather covering that reaches above the ankles and what is attached to it. The name derives from 'khiffah' (lightness) because the ruling is lightened from washing to wiping.
4
Memorize the prescribed durations
Resident: one day and one night (24 hours). Traveler: three days and three nights (72 hours). The duration starts from the first hadath after wearing the khuffs.
This is a common point of misunderstanding.
5
Note the legal basis and precedence
The passage states that wiping over khuffs is established by the Sunnah (according to the correct view). It is placed before tayammum because tayammum has basis in the Qur'an, while this has basis in the Sunnah, giving it precedence in the order.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب المسح على الخفين ذكره بعد التيمم لأن كلاً منهما طهارة مسح، وقدمه عليه لثبوته بالكتاب وهذا ثابت بالسنة على الصحيح كما سيأتي. والمسح لغة إمرار اليد على الشيء واصطلاحاً عبارة عن رخصة مقدرة جعلت للمقيم يوماً وليلة وللمسافر ثلاثة أيام ولياليها. والخف في الشرع اسم من الجلد الساتر للكعبين فصاعداً وما ألحق به، وسمي الخف خفاً من الخفة لأن الحكم خف به من الغسل إلى المسح.
Chapter on wiping over the khuffs. He mentioned it after tayammum because each of them is a purification by wiping. He gave it precedence over it because it is established by the Book (Qur'an) while this is established by the Sunnah according to the correct view, as will come. And mash linguistically is passing the hand over something; terminologically it is an expression for a limited concession made for the resident for a day and a night, and for the traveler for three days and their nights. And al-khuff in the Shari'ah is a term for leather covering the ankles and above, and what is attached to it. It is called khuff from lightness (khiffah) because the ruling is lightened from washing to wiping.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on wiping over khuffs. It explains why the author placed this chapter after tayammum: both involve wiping (mash), but wiping over khuffs is given precedence because it has basis in the Qur'an (according to some interpretations, though the text notes it is actually from Sunnah), while tayammum's primacy is by consensus. The author provides the linguistic and terminological definition of mash: a limited concession restricting the duration: one full day and night for a resident (muqim), three days and nights for a traveler. The khuff is defined as footwear that covers the ankles and upward, made of leather or similar. The term 'khuff' derives from 'khiffah' (lightness) because it alleviates the obligation from washing the feet to simply wiping.

Key Terms
المسح (al-mash): Passing wet hand over the khuff as a substitute for washing the feet in wudu
الخف (al-khuff): Leather foot covering that reaches above the ankles
رخصة مقدرة (rukhsah muqaddarah): A concession with a fixed limit (time duration)

Wiping Over Khuffs: Definition and the Source of Proof (Quran vs Sunnah)
Definition and proof of wiping over khuffs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the proof for wiping over khuffs and distinguish between the Quranic and Sunnah-based arguments.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuffs is proven by the Sunnah, not the Quran, according to the majority of Hanafis.

In this lesson, we explore the opening of the chapter on wiping over khuffs from al-Bahr al-Raiq. The commentator defines the key terms and then dives into a critical intra-madhhab dispute: does the permissibility come from the Quran or the Sunnah? Understanding this debate is essential for grasping the epistemological weight of the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon: wiping over khuffs. The hukm is ja'iz (permissible), not wajib, except in cases where washing would not suffice but wiping would.
The passage also defines the duration: muqim (resident) wipes for one day and night, musafir (traveller) for three days and nights.
2
Locate the Dalil
Two potential proofs are presented: the Quranic verse of wudu (with the jar reading) and the Sunnah. Identify which one is considered the actual dalil by the majority.
The jar reading (qira'ah bi al-jarr) is interpreted as wiping, but the majority reject this.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
For the Sunnah, the evidence is the abundance of hadiths (reaching tawatur) and the explicit statements of the Imams. For the Quran, the jar reading is explained as jar al-mujawarah (adjacency genitive).
The verse mentions 'to the ankles' which does not limit wiping, so the Quranic argument is weak.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf
Some Hanafis (e.g., in Ghayat al-Bayan) held the Quran proves wiping. The majority (جمهور مشايخنا) hold it is proven by the Sunnah. Identify the opposing view and its basis.
The disagreement is within the school, but the majority view is the mufta bihi.
5
Evaluate the Tarjih
The commentator adopts the majority view, as do the authors of al-Mustasfa and al-Mujma'. The tarjih is based on the strength of the Sunnah evidence and the weakness of the Quranic reading.
Abu Hanifa's strong statement ('I feared disbelief for the denier') reinforces the certainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

۲۸۸
كتاب الطهارة - باب المسح على الخفين
المسح، والثاني معرفة مدته والثالث معرفة الخف الذي يجوز عليه المسح، والرابع معرفة ما ينتقض به المسح والخامس معرفة حكمه إذا انتقض والسادس معرفة صورته وقد ذكرها المصنف فبدأ بالأول فقال (صح) أي جاز المسح على الخفين والصحة في العبادات على ما في التوضيح كونها بحيث توجب تفريغ الذمة فالمعتبر في مفهومها اعتباراً أولياً إنما هو المقصود الدنيوي وهو تفريغ الذمة وإن كان يلزمها الثواب مثلاً وهو المقصود الأخروي لكنه غير مقصود في مفهومه اعتباراً أولياً والوجوب كون الفعل بحيث لو أتى به يثاب ولو تركه يعاقب فالمعتبر في مفهومه اعتباراً أولياً هو المقصود الأخروي وإن كان يتبعه المقصود الدنيوي كتفريغ الذمة ونحوه .اهـ. واختلف مشايخنا جوازه ثابت بالكتاب أو بالسنة؟ فقيل بالكتاب عملاً بقراءة الجر فإنها لما عارضت قراءة النصب حملت على ما إذا كان متخففاً، وحملت قراءة النصب على ما إذا لم يكن متخففاً واختاره في غاية البيان، وقال الجمهور لم يثبت بالكتاب وهو الصحيح بدليل قوله إلى الكعبين لأن المسح غير مقدر بهذا بالإجماع، والصحيح أن جوازه ثبت بالسنة. كذا ذكره المصنف في المستصفى واختاره صاحب المجمع معللاً بأن الماسح على الخف ليس ماسحاً على الرجل حقيقة ولا حكماً لأن الخف اعتبر مانعاً سراية الحدث إلى القدم فهي طاهرة، وما حل بالخف أزيل بالمسح فهو على الخف حقيقة وحكماً، وحملوا قراءة الجر عطفاً على المغسول والجر للمجاورة وقد جاءت السنة بجوازه قولاً وفعلاً حتى قال أبو حنيفة : ما قلت بالمسح حتى جاءني فيه مثل ضوء النهار وعنه أخاف الكفر على من لم ير المسح على الخفين لأن الآثار التي جاءت فيه في حيز التواتر . وقال أبو يوسف : خبر المسح يجوز نسخ الكتاب به لشهرته وقال أحمد : ليس في قلبي شيء من المسح فيه أربعون حديثاً عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ما رفعوا وما وقفوا وعن الحسن البصري: أدركت سبعين نفراً من أصحاب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يرون المسح على الخفين ومن لم ير المسح عليهما جائزاً من الصحابة فقد صح رجوعهم كابن عباس وأبي هريرة وعائشة وقال شيخ الإسلام : الدليل على أن منكر المسح ضال مبتدع ما روي أن أبا حنيفة سأل عن مذهب أهل السنة والجماعة أن تفضل الشيخين وتحب الختنين وترى المسح على الخفين. وإنما لم يجعله واجباً لأن العبد مخير بين فعله وتركه، كذا قالوا .
فقال : هو
وينبغي أن يكون المسح واجباً في مواضع منها : إذا كان معه ماء لو غسل به رجليه لا يكفي وضوءه ولو مسح على الخفين يكفيه فإنه يتعين عليه المسح، ومنها ما لو خاف خروج
يقوم مقامها في الموضع المخصوص في المدة الشرعية . قوله : (هو أن تفضل الشيخين وتحب الختنين) المراد من الشيخين سيدنا أبو بكر وعمر رضي الله تعالى عنهما، ومن الختنين سيدنا عثمان وعلي رضي الله تعالى عنهما قوله : (وإنما لم يجعله أي المصنف.
Chapter on Wiping over Khuffs. He mentioned it after tayammum because each is a purification by wiping, and he gave it precedence because it is established by the Book (Quran) and this (wiping over khuffs) is established by the Sunnah according to the correct view, as will come. Linguistically, wiping (al-mash) is passing the hand over something. Terminologically, it is a limited concession granted to the resident for a day and a night and to the traveller for three days and their nights. The khuff in sacred law is a name for leather covering the ankles upwards and what is attached to it. It is named khuff from lightness because the ruling is lightened from washing to wiping. Then here one needs to know six things: first, knowing the origin of relying on this transmission... etc. Then the author said (is valid) meaning wiping over khuffs is permissible. And validity in acts of worship, according to what is in al-Tawdih, is that it brings about discharge of liability. So what is primarily considered in its concept is the worldly objective, which is discharge of liability, even though reward follows as a spiritual objective. Obligation is that the act is such that if one does it he is rewarded and if he leaves it he is punished. What is primarily considered in its concept is the spiritual objective. Our scholars differed: is its permissibility established by the Book or by the Sunnah? Some said by the Book, acting upon the reading with genitive case (jar), since when it contradicted the reading with accusative (nasb), it was interpreted as when one is not carrying footwear, and the accusative reading as when he is carrying footwear, as chosen in Ghayat al-Bayan. But the majority said it is not established by the Book — and this is correct — evidenced by His statement 'to the ankles' because wiping is not limited to this by consensus. And the correct view is that its permissibility is established by the Sunnah. Thus the author mentioned in al-Mustasfa and it was chosen by the author of al-Mujma', reasoning that the one wiping over the khuff is not wiping over the foot in reality or legally, because the khuff is considered as preventing the transmission of hadath to the foot, so the foot remains pure, and whatever reaches the khuff is removed by wiping; so wiping is on the khuff in reality and legally. They interpreted the genitive reading as a grammatical attachment to 'the washed parts' and the genitive is due to adjacency. And the Sunnah has come with its permissibility verbally and practically, until Abu Hanifa said: I did not say (the ruling of) wiping until clear evidence like daylight came to me. And from him: I fear disbelief for one who does not consider wiping over khuffs permissible, because the traditions regarding it are at the level of tawatur. Abu Yusuf said: The hadith of wiping permits abrogating the Book by it due to its widespread acceptance. Ahmad said: There is nothing in my heart (against) wiping; there are forty hadiths from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) about it — some marfu', some mawquf. Al-Hasan al-Basri said: I met seventy companions of the Messenger of Allah who considered wiping over khuffs permissible. And from among the Companions who did not consider it permissible, they have been reported to have retracted, such as Ibn Abbas, Abu Hurayra, and Aisha. Shaykh al-Islam said: Evidence that the denier of wiping is misguided and an innovator is what is narrated that Abu Hanifa was asked about the madhhab of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah: that you give preference to the two shaykhs, love the two sons-in-law, and consider wiping over khuffs permissible. And he did not make it obligatory because the servant is given choice between doing and leaving it, as they said. Then he said: It would be appropriate that wiping becomes obligatory in certain cases: if one has water that if he washes his feet with it it would not suffice for his wudu, but if he wipes over the khuffs it would suffice, then wiping becomes incumbent upon him; and also if he fears exiting... it takes its place in the specific place during the legal period. His statement: 'That you give preference to the two shaykhs and love the two sons-in-law' — the two shaykhs refer to our master Abu Bakr and Umar (may Allah be pleased with them), and the two sons-in-law refer to our master Uthman and Ali (may Allah be pleased with them). His statement: 'And he did not make it' meaning the author.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage is an introductory commentary on the chapter of wiping over khuffs from al-Bahr al-Raiq. The commentator begins by explaining why the chapter on wiping over khuffs is placed after tayammum: both involve purification by wiping, but he gave precedence to khuffs because its ruling is established by the Quran (according to some) while tayammum is established by the Sunnah. He then defines the key terms: 'mash' linguistically is passing the hand; terminologically it is a limited concession (rukhsah muqaddarah) — the resident wipes for one day and night, the traveler for three days and nights. 'Khuff' is a leather covering that conceals the ankles upwards. The ruling is lightened from washing to wiping. The author mentions six required knowledges for this chapter: (1) the origin of relying on the transmission about wiping, (2) its duration, (3) which khuffs are permissible to wipe over, (4) what nullifies the wiping, (5) its ruling when nullified, and (6) its specific manner. The commentator then discusses the author's statement 'sahha' (is valid), explaining that validity in worship means it discharges the liability (tafrig al-dhimmah) — the primary consideration is the worldly objective. Obligation (wujub) primarily concerns the spiritual objective of reward and punishment. Then a significant intra-Hanafi dispute is presented: some Hanafi scholars held that the permissibility of wiping over khuffs is proven by the Quran, acting upon the qira'ah bi al-jarr (the genitive reading in the verse of wudu). The majority, however, hold that it is not proven by the Quran but by the Sunnah, which is the correct position. The commentator supports this with several pieces of evidence: the verse mentions 'to the ankles' while wiping is not limited to that; the genitive reading is explained as jar al-mujawarah; and the Sunnah is replete with reports. He quotes Abu Hanifa's strong statement that he only accepted it after clear proof, and that he feared disbelief for its denier. Abu Yusuf noted that the hadith is so well-known it could abrogate the Quran. Imam Ahmad and al-Hasan al-Basri also affirmed the practice from companions. Finally, the commentator explains that wiping is not obligatory but a choice, though there are situations where it may become obligatory, such as when washing would not suffice the wudu but wiping would. This lesson establishes the reliability and mainstream acceptance of wiping over khuffs within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
المسح (al-mash): Passing a wet hand over the khuff or a specified limb; a limited concession (rukhsah muqaddarah) for purification.
الخف (al-khuff): A leather foot covering that conceals the ankles and above, including what is annexed to it like socks (jawrab) if they meet conditions.
المقيم (al-muqim): A resident who is not travelling; he wipes for one day and one night.
التيمم (al-tayammum): Dry purification with earth when water is unavailable; mentioned as similar to mash in being a wiping purification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi scholars, what is the source of the proof for the permissibility of wiping over khuffs?
A) The Quran, specifically the genitive reading (qira'ah bi al-jar) in the wudu verse
B) The Sunnah, as the Quran does not explicitly command wiping over khuffs
C) Consensus (ijma) of the companions
D) Rational analogy (qiyas) to tayammum

Key Takeaway
Wiping over khuffs is a proven practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) supported by mass-transmitted hadith; its proof is from the Sunnah, not the Quran, as upheld by the Hanafi school.

Validity and Obligation in Hanafi Fiqh
Defining validity and obligation in the context of wiping over socks.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'sahih' (valid) and 'wajib' (obligatory) as per Hanafi usul, and distinguish their primary purposes (dunyawi vs ukhtawi).

Core Idea
Validity is about discharging liability in this world; obligation is about reward and punishment in the next.

This lesson unpacks the opening of the chapter on wiping over socks, where the commentator explains the concepts of validity and obligation. Understanding these definitions is essential for grasping the legal weight of any act of worship in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two terms defined
The passage defines 'sahih' (valid) and 'wajib' (obligatory) for acts of worship. Find these terms and note the primary consideration for each.
The commentator cites al-Tawdih for definitions.
2
Differentiate the primary purpose
For validity, the primary purpose is worldly: discharge of liability (tafrigh al-dhimmah). For obligation, the primary purpose is otherworldly: reward and punishment.
Reward and punishment are the main focus of wajib, though it also discharges liability.
3
Apply to wiping over socks
The author states 'صح أي جاز المسح' meaning wiping is valid (sahih). It is not wajib because the servant is given a choice. Therefore, its primary effect is discharge of liability, not reward/punishment for leaving it.
4
Recognize the implication for fatwa
Knowing that wiping is not wajib means one may choose to wash the feet instead, and there is no sin for omitting wiping. This flexibility is a mercy in the school.
This ties back to the core idea.

Source Text
