عليه الثواب غير مسلم فإن أئمتنا إنما يريدون بمشروعية الفعل الجواز بحيث يترتب عليه أحكامه غير أن الثواب من جملة أحكام الفعل الذي يقصد به العبادة، فغسل الرجل حال التخفف لو لم يكن مشروعاً لما ترتب عليه حكمه من جواز الصلاة وغيرها مما تشترط له الطهارة واستدلاله بتنظيره من قصر الصلاة غير صحيح، فإن المسافر إذا صلى أربعاً وقعد على رأس الركعتين لا يكون آتياً بالعزيمة وليس في وسعه ذلك لأن فرضه ركعتان لا يطيق الزيادة عليهما فرضاً كما لا يطيق المقيم الزيادة على الأربع فرضاً، وإنما يتم فرضه ركعتين فحسب وأثم لبناء النفل وهو الركعتان الآخريان على تحريمة الفرض لا لأنه أتى بالعزيمة مع عدم جوازها وإباحتها له بخلاف المتخفف الذي انغسل أكثر رجله حيث اعتبر الغسل شرعاً وترتب عليه حكم من الأحكام الشرعية وهو بطلان المسح ولزوم نزع الخف لاتمام الغسل، ولو قدر أنه غسل كلتا الرجلين متخففاً لترتب عليه أنه لا ينتقض بتمام المدة ولا بنزع الخف مع جواز الأفعال التي تشترط لها الطهارة به فثبت مشروعية الغسل حال التخفف بمعنى تصوّر وجوده شرعاً وتحققه بخلاف الإتمام، واعتراض الزيلعي على أهل الأصول مقرر. وهذا كله على تقدير صحة الفرع الذي ذكره وهو منقول في الفتاوى الظهيرية وغيرها .اهـ. قال بعض الفضلاء وحاصله منع كون المسح رخصة إسقاط وإثبات من النوع الثاني من الرخصة وهو ما يرخص مع قيام السبب كفطر المسافر، وفي هذا النوع يجوز أنه في شرح الزاهدي في سياق نقله عن البحر المحيط. وعن أبي بكر العياضي: لا ينتقض وإن بلغ الماء الركبة اهـ . لكن ذكر في خير مطلوب لبس خفيه على الطهارة ومسح عليهما فدخل الماء إحداهما إن وصل الكعب حتى صار جميع الرجل مغسولاً يجب غسل الأخرى، وإن لم يبلغ الكعب لا ينتقض مسحه، وإن أصاب الماء أكثر إحدى رجليه اختلف فيه، فقد علمت صحة ما بحثه المحقق في فتح القدير غير أنه أقر القائل بأنه إذا انقضت المدة ولم يكن محدثاً لا يجب عليه غسل رجليه على هذا القول. وتعقبه تلميذه العلامة ابن أمير حاج بأنه يجب عليه غسل رجليه ثانياً إذا نزعهما أو انقضت المدة وهو غير محدث لأن عند النزع أو انقضاء المدة يعمل ذلك الحدث السابق عمله من السراية إلى الرجلين وقتئذ فيحتاج إلى مزيل له عنهما حينئذ للإجماع على أن المزيل لا يظهر عمله في حدث طار بعده فليتأمل اهـ.
By analogy to shortening prayer: if one performs the 'azima by praying four rak'ahs and sits after two rak'ahs, he sins even though his obligatory prayer is complete. The verification of its answer is that the one who avails a concession (mutarakhkhas) as long as he is in that state is not permitted to act by the 'azima. When the concession is removed, it is permissible for him to do so. So the traveler as long as he is traveling is not permitted to complete the prayer fully; if he begins with the intention of four, he must cut it and begin with two rak'ahs. If he begins with the intention of two and then intends to stay (i.e. no longer traveling) during the prayer, it becomes four. So the one in a state of alleviation (mutakhaffif) as long as he is in that state is not permitted to wash (his feet); if he forces himself and washes his feet without removing (the khuff), he sins, yet it suffices him for the washing. When he removes the khuff and the concession ceases, the washing becomes legitimate and he is rewarded for it. Astonishing that this is clear to one trained in the books of usul yet hidden from a great scholar... End. Know that 'azima is a ruling that is primary, not built on excuses, and rukhsa is built on excuses - this is the more correct definition among usul scholars. Know also that in Tatimmat al-Fatawa al-Sughra and in the Fatawa of Shaykh Imam Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl: if his foot becomes wet, his mash is not invalidated in any case because the covering of the foot by the khuff prevents the transmission of the hadath to the foot, so this (wetness) does not constitute considered washing, so it does not necessitate invalidation of the mash. This is supported by what... Their objection to them: let it be considered. End. His statement: (And the verification of his answer) meaning the answer of the author of al-Kafi, Imam al-Nasafi, as is known from al-Durar. It would have been appropriate for the author to use the plural form since he did not quote the exact expression. His statement: (Then he said in al-Sharnaballaliyya: regarding his sinning there is consideration, it is not hidden) His statement: (And astonishing...). Al-Allama al-Halabi answered him, saying after quoting what preceded from the author of al-Durar: I say: what he said about the meaning of legitimacy (mashru'iyya) being permissibility such that reward is reaped is not accepted. Our imams only mean by legitimacy of an act the permissibility such that its rulings are established, but reward is among the rulings of an act intended for worship. So washing the leg in a state of alleviation, if it were not legitimate, its ruling of permissibility of prayer and other conditions of purity would not apply. His deduction by analogy to shortening prayer is incorrect. For if the traveler prays four and sits after two rak'ahs, he is not performing the 'azima and it is not within his capacity because his obligation is two rak'ahs; he cannot add to them as an obligatory act, just as a resident cannot add to four as obligatory. Rather, his obligation is only two rak'ahs, and he sins because he built the supererogatory (the last two rak'ahs) upon the intention of the obligatory, not because he performed the 'azima while it was not permissible for him. Unlike the mutakhaffif who washed most of his foot; here the washing is considered legally and a ruling is attached to it, namely the invalidation of the mash and the necessity of removing the khuff to complete the washing. And if it were assumed that he washed both feet while in a state of alleviation, it would follow that (the mash) is not invalidated by the completion of the period nor by removing the khuff, along with permissibility of acts requiring purity. So the legitimacy of washing in a state of alleviation is established in the sense of its legal existence and realization, unlike completing the prayer. Al-Zayla'i's objection to the usul scholars is established. All this is based on the assumption of the correctness of the subsidiary case he mentioned, which is transmitted in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya and others. End. Some virtuous person said: its gist is the denial that mash is a rukhsa of removal and establishment from the second type of rukhsa, i.e., what is permitted while the cause exists, like the traveler breaking fast. In this type, it is permissible. In Sharh al-Zahidi in the context of his transmission from al-Bahr al-Muhit: From Abu Bakr al-'Iyadi: it is not invalidated even if water reaches the knee. End. But it is mentioned in Khayr Matlub: if one wears his khuffs with purity and wipes over them, then water enters one of them: if it reaches the ankle such that the entire foot becomes washed, it becomes obligatory to wash the other foot; if it does not reach the ankle, his mash is not invalidated. If water touches most of one of his feet, there is disagreement. You have known the correctness of what the muhaqqiq researched in Fath al-Qadir, except that he affirmed the statement that when the period expires and he is not in a state of hadath, he is not required to wash his feet according to this view. His student, the allama Ibn Amir Hajj, rebutted him saying that he must wash his feet a second time when he removes them or the period expires while he is not in hadath, because at removal or expiry of the period, that previous hadath acts by transmission to the feet at that time, so he needs to remove it from them then, due to consensus that the remover (washing) does not act on a hadath occurring after it. So let it be considered. End.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling of washing the feet while wearing khuffs (mash) when in a state of legal concession (rukhsa). The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the issue by analogizing to the traveler's prayer. The core ruling: if a person in a state of alleviation (mutakhaffif) washes his foot without removing the khuff, the act is valid (yujzi'u) but sinful (ya'tham). Once the khuff is removed and the concession ends, washing becomes fully recommended and rewarded. The passage then defines 'azima (primary ruling) and rukhsa (concession), citing usul sources. It also presents a fatwa from Tatimmat al-Fatawa al-Sughra that if the foot becomes wet without intentional washing, the mash is not invalidated because the khuff prevents transmission of hadath. The main dispute: Imam al-Zayla'i objected to the notion that washing while in takhaffuf is legitimate, arguing by analogy to the traveler completing prayer. Al-Halabi refutes this, showing that the cases differ: the traveler cannot 'complete' because his obligation is only two rak'ahs, whereas the mutakhaffif's washing is legally recognized and entails consequences (invalidating mash, requiring removal). The discussion includes further rulings on water entering the khuff after mash, with differences of opinion among Hanafi scholars. The author resolves that the correct view is that washing in takhaffuf is legitimate in the sense of legal existence, but not recommended.

Key Terms
عزيمة ('azima): Primary legal ruling not based on excuses, opposed to rukhsa.
رخصة (rukhsa): Concessionary ruling built on excuses, such as wiping over khuffs for travelers.
متخفف (mutakhaffif): One who is in a state of legal alleviation, e.g., wearing khuffs and therefore exempted from washing feet normally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a person in takhaffuf deliberately washes his foot without removing the khuff, what is the ruling?
A) The wudu is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The wudu is valid but he sins, and the mash is invalidated.
C) The wudu is valid and he is rewarded for his washing.
D) The wudu is invalid only if water reaches the ankle.

Key Takeaway
Washing the foot while in the state of takhaffuf is valid (yujzi'u) but sinful (ya'tham), and it invalidates the mash (مسح).

Women and the Ruling of Mash on Khuffs
Expansion on women's inclusion in mash ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that women are permitted to wipe over khuffs just like men and identify the textual basis for this ruling.

Core Idea
Women are equal to men in mash on khuffs; general texts include all.

This lesson addresses a specific expansion from the matn 'Kanz al-Daqa'iq': the word 'even a woman' (ولو امرأة). The commentator clarifies that the permission to wipe over khuffs is not restricted to men. This confirms that the general commands of the Qur'an and Sunnah regarding mash apply to both genders alike.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The text states 'wa law imra'a' — the ruling includes women. Understand that this is a permission (ibaha) for women to wipe over khuffs exactly like men.
2
Recognize the basis: generality of texts
The author says the ruling is due to the generality of the texts (itlaq al-nusus). In Hanafi usul, general texts cover all individuals unless a specification (takhsis) is proven. No such specification exists here.
3
Apply to all circumstances
The permission is not limited to travel or need; it applies whether one is a resident or traveler, with or without necessity.
4
Contrast with other schools
Note that some madhahib (e.g., Shafi'i) restrict mash to travelers, but the Hanafi view is that it is allowed for all, including women at home.
This is a thamarah al-khilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ولو امرأة) أي ولو كان الماسح امرأة لإطلاق النصوص، وقد قدمنا أن الخطاب الوارد في أحدهما يكون وارداً في حق الآخر ما لم ينص على التخصيص وأشار به إلى أنه يجوز للحاجة ولغيرها سفراً أو حضراً. قوله ( لا) جنباً) أي لا يجوز المسح على الخفين لمن وجب عليه الغسل، والمحققون على أن الموضع موضع النفي فلا حاجة إلى التصوير. وحاصله أنه إذا أجنب وقد لبس على وضوء وجب نزع خفيه وغسل رجليه . وذكر شمس الأئمة أن الجنابة ألزمته غسل جيمع البدن ومع الخف لا يتأتى ذلك . وفي الكفاية : صورته توضأ ولبس جوربين مجلدين ثم أجنب ليس له أن يشدهما ويغسل سائر جسده مضطجعاً ويمسح عليه اهـ. وبهذا اندفع ما في النهاية من أنه لا يتأتى الاغتسال مع وجود الخف ملبوساً، وقيل صورته مسافراً العمل بالعزيمة مع وجود الترخص لأن المسافر يجوز له أن يصوم في حال السفر ويثاب عليه، فالمتخفف إذا غسل رجليه حال التخفف يكون مشروعاً ويثاب عليه إذا لو لم يكن مشروعاً لما بطل مسحه إذا خاض الماء ودخل في الخف، ولما ترتب عليه حكمه، وأنت خبير إذا تأملت كلام المحقق كمال الدين وكلام صاحب الدرر علمت أن تنظير كل منهما في إشكال الزيلعي بملحظ غير ملحظ الآخر. فمحصل ما قاله المحقق منع صحة كلام الزيلعي ومنع صحة الفرع الذي استند إليه. ومحصل ما قاله صاحب الدرر صحة كلامه في ذاته ومنع وروده على النسفي والعلامة الحلبي منع منعه وأثبت وروده عليه وعلى من قال بقوله ورد كلام المحقق والله تعالى الموفق اهـ ملخصاً. لكن لا يخفى عليك ما في كلام الزيلعي والحلبي من نفي رخصة الإسقاط وادعاء أن ذلك من النوع الثاني فإن حكمه كما ذكر في الأصول أن الأخذ بالعزيمة أولى كفطر المسافر، والغسل حال التخفف ليس كذلك، ولهذا قال العلامة محمد القهستاني في شرحه على مختصر الوقاية وليس من رخصة الترفية في شيء إذا المعنى رخصة مخففة لجواز التأخير عن وقته للعذر وإن كان الأفضل أن لا يؤخر كقصر المسافر، فلو كان منها لزم أن يكون غسل المتخفف أفضل من مسحه، ولا يخفى ما في المقام من الكلام الوافي لتحقيق ما في الهداية والكافي فمن قال إن المسح رخصة ترفية عندهما فقد دل كلامه على بعد من
His statement: (And even a woman) meaning even if the one wiping is a woman, due to the generality of the texts. We have already stated that the address directed to one (gender) is directed to the other as well unless specialisation is mentioned. He indicated by this that it is permissible for need and without need, whether traveling or present. His statement: (not a junub) meaning it is not permissible to wipe over the khuffs for one upon whom ghusl is obligatory. The verifying scholars hold that the context is negation, so there is no need for (hypothetical) depiction. Its gist: if one becomes junub while he had worn (khuffs) in a state of wudu, he must remove his khuffs and wash his feet. Shams al-A'imma mentioned that janaba obligates washing the entire body, and with the khuff on, this cannot be achieved. In al-Kifaya: its depiction: he performed wudu and wore two leather socks (jurabayn mujalladayn), then became junub; he is not allowed to tighten them and wash the rest of his body lying down and wipe over them. End. By this is refuted what is in al-Nihaya that ghusl cannot be performed while the khuff is worn. And it was said: its depiction is a traveler... (continues discussion about 'azima and rukhsa, repeating earlier points).
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage provides two concise rulings from the matn (Kanz al-Daqa'iq). First, the rule that women are allowed to wipe over khuffs just like men, as the texts are general and not gender-specific. It is permitted for both travel and residence, and for need or no need. Second, a person in a state of major impurity (junub) is not permitted to wipe over khuffs; they must remove them and wash their feet as part of ghusl. The reason given is that janaba requires washing the entire body, which cannot be achieved with khuffs on. The author cites Shams al-A'imma al-Hulwani and al-Kifaya to support this. The passage then transitions back to the earlier discussion about the nature of rukhsa, repeating arguments from al-Halabi, al-Zayla'i, and al-Qahistani, but these are somewhat repetitive and may be a continuation from the previous lesson.

Key Terms
جنب (junub): One in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl (full body wash), e.g., after sexual intercourse or ejaculation.
مسح على الخفين (mash 'ala al-khuffayn): The act of wiping over leather socks with wet hands as a substitute for washing feet in wudu, subject to conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why are women permitted to wipe over khuffs?
A) Because it is a special concession for women.
B) Because the texts are general and there is no specification.
C) Because women are exempt from washing feet.
D) Because women only wear khuffs at home.

Key Takeaway
Women are permitted to wipe over khuffs just like men; the ruling is based on the generality of Islamic texts.

The Prohibition of Mash on Khuffs for the Junub
Ruling on junub and the obligation to remove khuffs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a person in a state of janaba (junub) cannot wipe over khuffs and must remove them for ghusl.

Core Idea
The junub must remove khuffs because janaba requires washing the entire body, which is impossible with khuffs on.

This lesson examines the second ruling from the same passage: a person who becomes junub while wearing khuffs must remove them and wash his feet as part of ghusl. The reason is that janaba requires complete washing of the entire body, and the khuffs prevent that. The passage provides authoritative support from Shams al-A'imma and al-Kifaya.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
The text says 'la junuban' — it is not permissible for the junub to wipe. He must remove the khuffs and wash his feet.
2
Understand the reason
Janaba requires washing the entire body (ghusl). With khuffs on, the feet are covered and cannot be washed properly.
3
Consider the depiction
The text gives a scenario: one performed wudu, wore khuffs, then became junub. He cannot simply wipe; he must remove them.
4
Distinguish from wudu
In wudu, wiping is a substitute for washing feet. In janaba, there is no substitute; all parts must be washed directly.
5
Apply the principle
If someone becomes junub while in a state of wudu with khuffs, they must remove khuffs and perform ghusl, including washing the feet.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ولو امرأة) أي ولو كان الماسح امرأة لإطلاق النصوص، وقد قدمنا أن الخطاب الوارد في أحدهما يكون وارداً في حق الآخر ما لم ينص على التخصيص وأشار به إلى أنه يجوز للحاجة ولغيرها سفراً أو حضراً. قوله ( لا) جنباً) أي لا يجوز المسح على الخفين لمن وجب عليه الغسل، والمحققون على أن الموضع موضع النفي فلا حاجة إلى التصوير. وحاصله أنه إذا أجنب وقد لبس على وضوء وجب نزع خفيه وغسل رجليه . وذكر شمس الأئمة أن الجنابة ألزمته غسل جيمع البدن ومع الخف لا يتأتى ذلك . وفي الكفاية : صورته توضأ ولبس جوربين مجلدين ثم أجنب ليس له أن يشدهما ويغسل سائر جسده مضطجعاً ويمسح عليه اهـ. وبهذا اندفع ما في النهاية من أنه لا يتأتى الاغتسال مع وجود الخف ملبوساً، وقيل صورته مسافراً العمل بالعزيمة مع وجود الترخص لأن المسافر يجوز له أن يصوم في حال السفر ويثاب عليه، فالمتخفف إذا غسل رجليه حال التخفف يكون مشروعاً ويثاب عليه إذا لو لم يكن مشروعاً لما بطل مسحه إذا خاض الماء ودخل في الخف، ولما ترتب عليه حكمه، وأنت خبير إذا تأملت كلام المحقق كمال الدين وكلام صاحب الدرر علمت أن تنظير كل منهما في إشكال الزيلعي بملحظ غير ملحظ الآخر. فمحصل ما قاله المحقق منع صحة كلام الزيلعي ومنع صحة الفرع الذي استند إليه. ومحصل ما قاله صاحب الدرر صحة كلامه في ذاته ومنع وروده على النسفي والعلامة الحلبي منع منعه وأثبت وروده عليه وعلى من قال بقوله ورد كلام المحقق والله تعالى الموفق اهـ ملخصاً. لكن لا يخفى عليك ما في كلام الزيلعي والحلبي من نفي رخصة الإسقاط وادعاء أن ذلك من النوع الثاني فإن حكمه كما ذكر في الأصول أن الأخذ بالعزيمة أولى كفطر المسافر، والغسل حال التخفف ليس كذلك، ولهذا قال العلامة محمد القهستاني في شرحه على مختصر الوقاية وليس من رخصة الترفية في شيء إذا المعنى رخصة مخففة لجواز التأخير عن وقته للعذر وإن كان الأفضل أن لا يؤخر كقصر المسافر، فلو كان منها لزم أن يكون غسل المتخفف أفضل من مسحه، ولا يخفى ما في المقام من الكلام الوافي لتحقيق ما في الهداية والكافي فمن قال إن المسح رخصة ترفية عندهما فقد دل كلامه على بعد من
His statement: (And even a woman) meaning even if the one wiping is a woman, due to the generality of the texts. We have already stated that the address directed to one (gender) is directed to the other as well unless specialisation is mentioned. He indicated by this that it is permissible for need and without need, whether traveling or present. Second, a person in a state of major impurity (junub) is not permitted to wipe over khuffs; they must remove them and wash their feet as part of ghusl. The reason given is that janaba requires washing the entire body, which cannot be achieved with khuffs on. The author cites Shams al-A'imma al-Hulwani and al-Kifaya to support this. The passage then transitions back to the earlier discussion about the nature of rukhsa, repeating arguments from al-Halabi, al-Zayla'i, and al-Qahistani, but these are somewhat repetitive and may be a continuation from the previous lesson.

Key Terms
جنب (junub): One in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl (full body wash), e.g., after sexual intercourse or ejaculation.
مسح على الخفين (mash 'ala al-khuffayn): The act of wiping over leather socks with wet hands as a substitute for washing feet in wudu, subject to conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He may wipe over the khuffs without removing them.
B) He must remove the khuffs and wash his feet as part of ghusl.
C) He may keep the khuffs on and perform ghusl without removing them.
D) He must repeat his wudu but can keep the khuffs on.

Key Takeaway
A junub cannot wipe over khuffs; he must remove them because janaba requires washing the entire body.

Effect of Water Inside the Khuff and Expiry of Wiping Period
Intra-Hanafi dispute on khuff wipe invalidation and expiry

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which water entering the khuff invalidates the wipe, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether foot washing is required after the wipe period expires without new hadath.

Core Idea
Water reaching the anklebone inside the khuff invalidates the wipe on that foot; but whether the original hadath returns after expiry is disputed.

This lesson delves into a nuanced intra-Hanafi debate about the effect of water entering the leather sock (khuff) during the wiping period, and what happens when the period expires without a new ritual impurity (hadath). The passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents conflicting views from early and later Hanafi authorities, culminating in a sharp critique by Ibn Amir Hajj of the position affirmed in Fath al-Qadir. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to trace the reasoning behind different Hanafi opinions and recognize the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two legal issues
The passage discusses two separate but related issues: (1) water entering the khuff during the wipe period, and (2) what happens when the wipe period expires without a new hadath. Identify each
The first issue involves invalidation of the wipe; the second involves return of the original hadath obligation.
2
State the ruling for water entry according to Khiyar Mahlub
If water reaches the anklebone (ka'b) and wets the entire foot, that foot is effectively washed, invalidating the wipe on that foot; the other foot must then be washed. If water does not reach the anklebone, the wipe remains valid.
The key condition is the water reaching the ka'b, not merely moistening part of the foot.
3
Contrast with Abu Bakr al-'Iyadi's absolute view
Another Hanafi authority, Abu Bakr al-'Iyadi, held that water entering the khuff does not invalidate the wipe even if it reaches the knee. This shows that even within the school there is disagreement on the threshold.
Al-Zahidi transmits this from al-Bahr al-Muhit.
4
Analyze the dispute on expiry of the wiping period
The commentator notes that the muhaqqiq (author of Fath al-Qadir) affirmed that if the period expires and the person has not nullified wudu, he does not need to wash his feet. Ibn Amir Hajj criticizes this, arguing that upon removal or expiry, the previous hadath becomes effective and spreads to the feet, necessitating washing.
Ibn Amir Hajj's reasoning relies on a consensus that the remover (wipe) does not affect a hadath occurring after it.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Under the Fath al-Qadir view, one can simply remove the khuffs and remain pure. Under Ibn Amir Hajj's view, one must perform a fresh washing of the feet (or a complete wudu) immediately upon removal or expiry.
This difference affects daily practice for those who wipe over khuffs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في شرح الزاهدي في سياق نقله عن البحر المحيط. وعن أبي بكر العياضي: لا ينتقض وإن بلغ الماء الركبة اهـ . لكن ذكر في خير مطلوب لبس خفيه على الطهارة ومسح عليهما فدخل الماء إحداهما إن وصل الكعب حتى صار جميع الرجل مغسولاً يجب غسل الأخرى، وإن لم يبلغ الكعب لا ينتقض مسحه، وإن أصاب الماء أكثر إحدى رجليه اختلف فيه، فقد علمت صحة ما بحثه المحقق في فتح القدير غير أنه أقر القائل بأنه إذا انقضت المدة ولم يكن محدثاً لا يجب عليه غسل رجليه على هذا القول. وتعقبه تلميذه العلامة ابن أمير حاج بأنه يجب عليه غسل رجليه ثانياً إذا نزعهما أو انقضت المدة وهو غير محدث لأن عند النزع أو انقضاء المدة يعمل ذلك الحدث السابق عمله من السراية إلى الرجلين وقتئذ فيحتاج إلى مزيل له عنهما حينئذ للإجماع على أن المزيل لا يظهر عمله في حدث طار بعده فليتأمل اهـ.
In the commentary of al-Zahidi, in the context of his transmission from al-Bahr al-Muhit: From Abu Bakr al-'Iyadi: It is not invalidated even if water reaches the knee. But it is mentioned in Khiyar Mahlub: He wore his khuffs with purification and wiped over them, then water entered one of them. If it reached the anklebone so that the entire foot became washed, the other foot must be washed. If it did not reach the anklebone, his wipe is not invalidated. If water affected most of one of his feet, there is disagreement about it. You have known the correctness of what the muhaqqiq verified in Fath al-Qadir, except that he affirmed the one who says that when the period expires and he is not in a state of hadath, he is not obligated to wash his feet according to this statement. His student, the scholar Ibn Amir Hajj, criticizes him by saying that he must wash his feet for a second time when he removes them or when the period expires while he is not in a state of hadath, because upon removal or expiry, that previous hadath takes effect, spreading to the feet at that time, so he needs a remover for it from them at that time, due to consensus that the remover does not take effect for a hadath that occurs after it. So reflect. End.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of water entering the khuff during the period of wiping. The commentator begins by citing al-Zahidi, who relates from al-Bahr al-Muhit the view of Abu Bakr al-'Iyadi that the wipe is not invalidated even if water reaches the knee. Then he mentions a contrary view from Khiyar Mahlub: if water reaches the anklebone and wets the entire foot, the foot is effectively washed, thus the wipe on that foot is invalidated and the other foot must be washed; if water does not reach the anklebone, the wipe remains valid. When water affects most of one foot, there is disagreement among scholars. The commentator then discusses the verification by the author of Fath al-Qadir, who affirmed the position that when the period of wiping expires and the person is not in a state of hadath (i.e., had not nullified his wudu after wiping), he is not required to wash his feet. This is criticized by Ibn Amir Hajj, who argues that upon removing the khuffs or expiry of the period, the previous hadath (which existed before the wipe) becomes operative and spreads to the feet, thus requiring the feet to be washed anew. He supports this by a consensus that the remover (i.e., the wipe) does not affect a hadath that occurs after it. The commentator concludes with 'let one ponder,' indicating the depth of the debate. The core issue is whether the original obligation of washing the feet is suspended by the wipe or merely deferred; Ibn Amir Hajj holds that if the wipe ceases without a new wudu, the original hadath returns and must be removed by washing.

Key Terms
خف (khuff): Leather socks that can be wiped over in place of washing the feet wudū'.
كعب (ka'b): Anklebone; the point up to which the foot must be washed in wudū'.
حدث (hadath): Ritual impurity that nullifies wudū' (minor hadath).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the view of Ibn Amir Hajj, what is the ruling when the wipe period expires without a new hadath?
A) The person remains pure and does not need to wash his feet.
B) The person must wash his feet because the previous hadath returns.
C) The person must perform a complete new wudu.
D) The person may choose to wash or not.

Key Takeaway
The effect of water entering the khuff depends on reaching the anklebone; the return of hadath after the wipe period expires is a contested issue within the Hanafi school.

Rulings on Women and Junub Regarding Wiping over Khuffs
Statements that women may wipe and junub may not

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi rulings on wiping over khuffs for women and a junub, and explain the legal reasoning for each.

Core Idea
Women may wipe over khuffs like men; junub must remove them because ghusl requires full foot washing.

In Hanafi fiqh, wiping over khuffs is a concession for wudu, but it is not unconditional. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies two important points: women are fully included in the concession, while a person in major impurity (junub) is excluded. The rulings hinge on the general applicability of the texts and the specific requirements of ghusl.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Locate the two direct statements: 'even a woman' indicates permissibility; 'not a junub' indicates prohibition.
The text uses concise phrasing: 'ولو امرأة' and 'لا جنباً'.
2
Understand the reasoning for women
The commentary states that the general texts about wiping apply to both men and women unless there is a specification excluding women. Since no such specification exists, women are included.
This is based on the usul principle that an address to one gender applies to the other unless explicitly restricted.
3
Understand the reasoning for junub
A junub must perform ghusl, which requires washing the entire body, including the feet. The khuff prevents water from reaching the feet, so wiping over them is invalid. The junub must remove the khuffs and wash the feet.
Even if physically possible to wash around the khuff, the concession of wiping is not granted for ghusl.
4
Refute the contrary view
The text refutes the claim in al-Nihayah that ghusl is impossible with the khuff on. It asserts that one could wash the rest of the body while wearing khuffs, but the point is that wiping is not allowed, not that ghusl is impossible.
The refutation preserves the logical consistency of the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ولو امرأة) أي ولو كان الماسح امرأة لإطلاق النصوص، وقد قدمنا أن الخطاب الوارد في أحدهما يكون وارداً في حق الآخر ما لم ينص على التخصيص وأشار به إلى أنه يجوز للحاجة ولغيرها سفراً أو حضراً. قوله ( لا) جنباً) أي لا يجوز المسح على الخفين لمن وجب عليه الغسل، والمحققون على أن الموضع موضع النفي فلا حاجة إلى التصوير. وحاصله أنه إذا أجنب وقد لبس على وضوء وجب نزع خفيه وغسل رجليه . وذكر شمس الأئمة أن الجنابة ألزمته غسل جيمع البدن ومع الخف لا يتأتى ذلك . وفي الكفاية : صورته توضأ ولبس جوربين مجلدين ثم أجنب ليس له أن يشدهما ويغسل سائر جسده مضطجعاً ويمسح عليه اهـ. وبهذا اندفع ما في النهاية من أنه لا يتأتى الاغتسال مع وجود الخف ملبوساً، وقيل صورته مسافراً
His statement: 'Even a woman' - meaning even if the one wiping is a woman, due to the general application of the texts. We have previously stated that the address directed to one of them is addressed to the other unless specification is stated. He alluded by this that it is permissible for necessity and otherwise, whether traveling or residing. His statement: 'Not a junub' - meaning it is not permissible to wipe over the khuffs for one upon whom ghusl is obligatory. The verifying scholars hold that the context is one of negation, so there is no need for illustration. Its summary is that if he becomes junub while he had worn them with wudu, he must remove his khuffs and wash his feet. Shams al-A'imma mentioned that janabah necessitates washing the entire body, and with the khuff that cannot be achieved. End. And by this, what is in al-Nihayah is refuted: that it is not possible to perform ghusl with the khuff worn. It was said: Its form is a traveler...

Commentary
This passage states two clear rulings: first, women are permitted to wipe over khuffs just as men are, because the texts are general and no specification excludes them. The permissibility applies whether in need or not, traveling or at home. Second, a person in a state of major ritual impurity (junub) is not permitted to wipe over khuffs, even if he had worn them while in wudu. The reason is that janabah requires a full body wash (ghusl), and the presence of khuffs prevents water from reaching the feet. Therefore, he must remove the khuffs and wash his feet as part of ghusl. The commentator refutes the suggestion in al-Nihayah that ghusl is impossible with the khuff on; rather, one could wash the rest of the body, but wiping is not allowed. The ruling is clear: junub cannot wipe over khuffs.

Key Terms
جنب (junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.
جوربين مجلدين (jurabayn mujalladayn): Two leather socks (jurab) that are thick or reinforced, similar to khuffs.

Women may wipe over khuffs based on general texts; a junub must remove khuffs for ghusl because wiping cannot substitute washing the feet.

Wiping over Khuffs after Tayammum: The Requirement of Complete Purification
Detailed scenario of a junub who uses tayammum, wears khuffs, then has minor hadath and finds water.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition that wiping over khuffs is only valid when the khuffs are worn after a complete purification with water, and apply this condition to scenarios involving tayammum.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuffs is only valid when worn after water purification, not after tayammum.

This lesson examines a nuanced scenario: a person in major impurity (janabah) performs tayammum due to lack of water, then wears khuffs, later has a minor hadath, and finds water. Can he wipe? The Hanafi ruling is clear: no, because tayammum is not a complete purification. The passage from Bahr al-Raiq explains this and discusses the sequence of events, citing the hadith of Safwan and the principle that wiping is a concession limited to its textual basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its subject
The passage addresses the permissibility of wiping over khuffs after wearing them following tayammum. First, identify the act (wiping) and the ruling in this specific scenario.
The ruling is that wiping is NOT permissible; the khuffs must be removed.
2
Examine the condition for valid wiping
The passage states that wiping is only valid if the khuffs were worn after a complete purification (taharah kamilah), i.e., with water. Tayammum does not qualify, as it does not purify the feet fully for the purpose of khuffs.
This condition is derived from the hadith and the principle that wiping is an exception to analogy.
3
Trace the dalil and its wajh al-dalalah
The passage references the hadith of Safwan (reported by al-Tirmidhi and al-Nasa'i) which prohibits wiping for a junub. The evidence points to the need for complete purification.
The hadith is ahad, so the ruling is based on zanni evidence.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some commentators of al-Hidayah criticized the scenario as unnecessary complexity. However, Fath al-Qadir affirms the condition, explaining that wiping is contrary to qiyas and must be strictly limited to the prophetic practice.
This shows the importance of adhering to the source text without expansion.
5
Apply the condition to the full scenario
Work through the steps: initial tayammum → wearing khuffs → minor hadath → finding water → rule: remove khuffs, wash feet. Then subsequent events: after re-wearing on water purification, wiping is valid; later janabah from abundant water breaks the condition again.
The sequence illustrates how the condition applies dynamically.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تيمم جنب ولا ماء عنده فتيمم ولبس ثم أحدث ووجد ماء يكفي وضوءه لا يجوز له المسح لأن الجنابة سرت إلى القدمين والتيمم ليس بطهارة كاملة فلا يجوز له المسح إذا لبسهما على طهارته فينزعهما ويغسلهما، فإذا فعل ولبس ثم أحدث وعنده ماء يكفي للوضوء توضأ ومسح لأن هذا الحدث يمنعه الخف السراية لوجوده بعد اللبس على طهارة كاملة، فلو مر بعد ذلك بماء كثير عاد جنباً، فإذا لم يغتسل حتى فقده له، فإذا أحدث ذلك بعد وعنده ماء يكفي للوضوء توضأ وغسل رجليه لأن عاد جنباً، فإن أحدث بعد ذلك وعنده ما للوضوء فقط توضأ ومسح وعلى هذا تجرى المسائل. وقد ذكر شراح الهداية أن هذا تكلف غير محتاج إليه. وفي فتح القدير أنه يفيد أنه يشترط لجواز المسح كون اللبس على طهارة الماء لا طهارة التيمم معللاً بأن طهارة التيمم ليست بطهارة كاملة، فإن أريد بعدم كمالها عدم الرفع عن الرجلين فهو ممنوع، وإن أريد عدم اصابة الرجلين في الوظيفة حساً فيمنع تأثيره في نفي الكمال المعتبر في الطهارة التي يعقبها اللبس. ويمكن أن يوجه الحكم المذكور بأن المسح على خلاف القياس، وإنما ورد من فعله هو على طهارة الماء ولم يرد من قوله ما يوسع مورده فيلزم فيه الماء قصراً على مورد الشرع، وحديث صفوان صريح في منعه للجنابة .اهـ. وهو ما رواه الترمذي والنسائي وابن
A junub with no water performed tayammum and wore [khuffs], then had a minor hadath and found water sufficient for his wudu. He is not permitted to wipe because janabah has spread to the feet, and tayammum is not a complete purification, so he is not permitted to wipe if he wears them with his purification. He must remove them and wash his feet. If he does that and wears them, then has a minor hadath and has water sufficient for wudu, he performs wudu and wipes because this hadath prevents the spread of the khuff due to its occurring after wearing on a complete purification. If after that he passes by abundant water, he becomes junub again. If he does not perform ghusl until he loses it, then if he has a hadath after that and has only enough water for wudu, he performs wudu and washes his feet because he became junub. If he has a hadath after that and has only enough for wudu, he performs wudu and wipes. And upon this, the cases proceed. The commentators of al-Hidayah have said that this is an unnecessary affectation. In Fath al-Qadir, it states that it shows that for the permissibility of wiping, the wearing must be on purification with water, not tayammum, reasoned that tayammum is not a complete purification. If by incompleteness is meant that it does not remove hadith from the feet, it is disallowed; if it is meant that the feet are not physically touched in the duty, it prevents its effect in negating the perfection considered in the purification after which wearing occurs. It is possible to justify the mentioned ruling by saying wiping is contrary to analogy, and it is reported only from his action upon purification with water, and no statement from him broadens its source, so it is limited to the source of sharia. The hadith of Safwan is explicit in prohibiting it for the junub. End. And it is what al-Tirmidhi and al-Nasa'i and Ibn...

Commentary
This passage tackles a complex scenario involving a junub person who uses tayammum due to lack of water, then wears khuffs, then has a minor hadath, then finds water, etc. The ruling: if he wore the khuffs after tayammum, he cannot wipe over them because tayammum is not a complete purification like wudu with water. The janabah has already affected the feet, and tayammum does not fully purify them. Therefore, he must remove the khuffs and wash his feet. If he then performs wudu with water and wears the khuffs again, he can wipe later because now the wearing is upon a complete purification. The passage also discusses a situation where he becomes junub again after seeing water, and the sequence of events. The commentators of al-Hidayah criticized this as unnecessary complexity. The author of Fath al-Qadir explains that the condition for valid wiping is that the wearing occurs after a purification with water, not tayammum, because wiping is a departure from analogy (qiyas) and is limited to the specific practice of the Prophet (ﷺ), who only performed it after water purification. The hadith of Safwan (reported by al-Tirmidhi and al-Nasa'i) explicitly prohibits wiping for a junub. The passage underscores that wiping is a concession that cannot be extended beyond its textual basis.

Key Terms
تيمم (tayammum): Dry purification with clean earth when water is unavailable or harmful.
طهارة كاملة (taharah kamilah): Complete purification, i.e., wudu or ghusl with water, as opposed to tayammum.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He may wipe over his khuffs because tayammum is a valid purification.
B) He must remove his khuffs and wash his feet with water.
C) He may wipe over his khuffs only if he intended to travel.
D) He must repeat the tayammum before wiping.

Key Takeaway
Wiping over khuffs requires that the khuffs be worn after a complete purification with water; tayammum does not suffice.

Invalidity of Wiping over Khuffs After Tayammum for Janabah
Establishes ruling and proof for junub who tayammum, wears khuffs, then finds water for wudu only.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping over khuffs when worn after tayammum for janabah, and explain the proof from the hadith of Safwan.

Core Idea
Tayammum is not complete purification; khuffs worn after tayammum do not permit wiping.

This lesson examines a specific scenario: a person in major ritual impurity (junub) who performs tayammum, wears khuffs, and later finds only enough water for wudu. The Hanafi school rules that he cannot wipe over the khuffs. Through the hadith of Safwan and the concept of 'complete purification', we will understand why this position is taken and how it differs from other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
Clearly state the situation: a junub person has no water, performs tayammum, wears khuffs, then has a minor hadath and finds water sufficient only for wudu. The ruling: he cannot wipe over the khuffs; he must remove them and wash his feet.
This is the primary ruling in the passage.
2
Understand the reason: tayammum is not complete purification
The text gives the reason: 'because the state of major impurity has reached the feet and tayammum is not a complete purification'. Tayammum for janabah does not purify the feet in a way that satisfies the condition for khuff wiping.
Contrast with complete purification (wudu or ghusl with water) which does satisfy.
3
Examine the hadith proof
The hadith of Safwan ibn 'Assal explicitly excludes janabah from the concession of wiping over khuffs: '... except from janabah, but from urine, feces, and sleep.' This shows that the concession is only for minor impurities.
The hadith is narrated by multiple reliable sources and considered sound.
4
Trace the subsequent scenarios
The passage explores various outcomes depending on water availability and state. This reinforces the principle that the key condition is wearing khuffs after complete purification (water-based). Once the condition is met, wiping for minor hadath is valid; if janabah reoccurs, the khuffs must be removed again.
The detailed scenarios illustrate the practical application of the principle.
5
Evaluate the difference between major and minor impurity
The central point: khuff wiping is a concession for minor impurities only. Janabah, even if purified by tayammum, still prevents wiping because tayammum does not fully remove the effect of janabah from the feet according to the Hanafi view.
This distinguishes the Hanafi position from schools that consider tayammum as fully lifting janabah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جنب ولا ماء عنده فتيمم ولبس ثم أحدث ووجد ماء يكفي وضوءه لا يجوز له المسح لأن الجنابة سرت إلى القدمين والتيمم ليس بطهارة كاملة فلا يجوز له المسح إذا لبسهما على طهارته فينزعهما ويغسلهما، فإذا فعل ولبس ثم أحدث وعنده ماء يكفي للوضوء توضأ ومسح لأن هذا الحدث يمنعه الخف السراية لوجوده بعد اللبس على طهارة كاملة، فلو مر بعد ذلك بماء كثير عاد جنباً، فإذا لم يغتسل حتى فقده له، فإذا أحدث ذلك بعد وعنده ماء يكفي للوضوء توضأ وغسل رجليه لأن عاد جنباً، فإن أحدث بعد ذلك وعنده ما للوضوء فقط توضأ ومسح وعلى هذا تجرى المسائل. وقد ذكر شراح الهداية أن هذا تكلف غير محتاج إليه. وفي فتح القدير أنه يفيد أنه يشترط لجواز المسح كون اللبس على طهارة الماء لا طهارة التيمم معللاً بأن طهارة التيمم ليست بطهارة كاملة، فإن أريد بعدم كمالها عدم الرفع عن الرجلين فهو ممنوع، وإن أريد عدم اصابة الرجلين في الوظيفة حساً فيمنع تأثيره في نفي الكمال المعتبر في الطهارة التي يعقبها اللبس. ويمكن أن يوجه الحكم المذكور بأن المسح على خلاف القياس، وإنما ورد من فعله هو على طهارة الماء ولم يرد من قوله ما يوسع مورده فيلزم فيه الماء قصراً على مورد الشرع، وحديث صفوان صريح في منعه للجنابة .اهـ. وهو ما رواه الترمذي والنسائي وابن ماجه وابن حبان وابن خزيمة بسند صحيح عن صفوان بن عسال قال : كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يأمرنا إذا كنا سفراً أن لا ننزع خفافنا ثلاثة أيام ولياليها لا عن جنابة ولكن عن بول وغائط ونوم. وروي إلا من جنابة في كتب الحديث المشهورة، وروي بحرف النفي وكلاهما صحيح ولكن المشهور رواية (إلا)) الاستثنائية . ووقع في كتب الفقه ولكن عن بول أو غائط أو نوم» بـ«أو» والمشهور في كتب الحديث بالواو . كذا ذكر النووي.
[A] person in a state of major ritual impurity (junub) and there is no water with him, so he performs tayammum and wears [khuffs], then he has a minor event (hadath) and finds water sufficient for wudu: it is not permissible for him to wipe [over the khuffs] because the state of major impurity has reached the feet and tayammum is not a complete purification. So he must remove them and wash [his feet]. If he does that and wears [them again] then has a minor event and has water sufficient for wudu, he performs wudu and wipes because this minor event is prevented by the khuff from reaching [the feet] since it occurred after wearing them upon a complete purification. If after that he passes by abundant water, he becomes junub again. If he does not perform ghusl until he loses it [the water], then he has that minor event after that and has water sufficient only for wudu, he performs wudu and washes his feet because he has become junub. Then if he has a minor event after that and has only enough water for wudu, he performs wudu and wipes. And upon this the cases proceed. The commentators of al-Hidayah have said that this is unnecessary complication. And in Fath al-Qadir that it indicates that for the permissibility of wiping, it is required that the wearing be upon water purification, not tayammum purification, reasoned that tayammum is not a complete purification. If by incompleteness is meant the lack of removal from the feet, it is denied; if it means the lack of actually reaching the feet in the function, it prevents its effect in negating the completeness considered in the purification after which the wearing occurs. It is possible to justify the mentioned ruling by [saying] that wiping is contrary to analogy, and it is only transmitted from his action upon water purification, and nothing from his speech broadens its scope, so water is restricted only to the scope of the Law, and the hadith of Safwan is explicit in preventing it for janabah. And it is what al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa'i, Ibn Majah, Ibn Hibban, and Ibn Khuzaymah narrated with a sound chain from Safwan ibn 'Assal who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to command us when we were traveling not to remove our khuffs for three days and nights except from janabah, but from urine, feces, and sleep. And it is narrated as 'except from janabah' in famous hadith books, and narrated with the letter of negation, both are authentic, but the famous narration is with the exceptive 'illa'. And it occurs in fiqh books as 'but from urine or feces or sleep' with 'aw', but the famous in hadith books is with 'waw'. Al-Nawawi mentioned this.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof. The author presents a detailed series of scenarios involving a person who is junub, performs tayammum, and wears khuffs. The core ruling is that if such a person later has a minor hadath and finds water sufficient only for wudu, he cannot wipe over the khuffs; he must remove them and wash his feet. The reason given is that tayammum is not a complete purification—it does not remove the effect of janabah from the feet, so the khuffs were not worn after a complete purification, which is a condition for valid wiping. The text then explores further scenarios where the person removes the khuffs, washes his feet, and wears them again after having water for wudu. In that case, if he later has a minor hadath, he may wipe because now the khuffs were worn after a complete (water) purification. However, if after that he encounters abundant water, he becomes junub again, and must perform ghusl; if he does not and later has a minor hadath, he must wash his feet again. The commentators note that this chain of scenarios is unnecessarily complicated. Fath al-Qadir explains that the condition for valid wiping is that the khuffs be worn after water purification, not tayammum, because tayammum is incomplete. The proof is the hadith of Safwan ibn 'Assal, which explicitly exempts janabah from the concession of wiping over khuffs. The hadith indicates that the concession applies only to minor impurities, not major ones. Thus, the ruling is firmly grounded in the primary textual evidence.

Key Terms
تيمم (tayammum): Dry purification using clean earth in place of wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
خف (khuff): A leather sock covering the foot and ankle, worn over the foot, upon which wiping is permissible under conditions.
جنابة (janabah): Major ritual impurity requiring ghusl, arising from sexual intercourse or ejaculation.
حدث (hadath): Minor ritual impurity that invalidates wudu, such as urination, defecation, or sleep.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, if a junub person performs tayammum, wears khuffs, then finds water only enough for wudu, can he wipe over his khuffs?
A) Yes, because tayammum is a valid purification.
B) Yes, because the water is only for wudu, not ghusl.
C) No, because tayammum is not a complete purification for the feet.
D) No, because he must perform ghusl first.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum does not constitute complete purification for the condition of khuff wiping; thus wiping after janabah is invalid in the Hanafi school.

Effect of Water Entering the Khuff on Wiping
Intra-Hanafi dispute on water entering khuff

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on water entering the khuff and apply the mufta bihi ruling to determine wipe validity.

Core Idea
Wetting most of the foot inside the khuff nullifies the wipe; less than three fingers does not.

You are about to explore a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: what happens when water enters the khuff during wudu? The answer is not simple—there are multiple views among Hanafi scholars. This lesson will guide you through the opinions of Abu Hanifa, later mashayikh, and the relied-upon position for fatwa. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to weigh evidence and identify the mufta bihi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core act and question
The act is wiping over khuffs (mash ala al-khuffayn). The question: does water entering the khuff and wetting the foot invalidate the wipe?
This is a dispute because water reaching the foot could be considered a removal of the khuff's preventer.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that if the entire foot (up to the ankle) becomes wet, the wipe is invalid. If only a small amount (three fingers or less) is wet, the wipe remains valid.
This is from zahir al-riwayah.
3
Present the variant opinions
Abu Ja'far and some mashayikh say wetting most of one foot nullifies the wipe. Others say it never nullifies the wipe regardless of how much water enters.
These are recorded in later fatwa collections like al-Tatarkhaniyyah and al-Dhakhira.
4
Identify the mufta bihi
Al-Zayla'i and al-Marghinani prefer the view that washing most of the foot nullifies the wipe. This is the most sound position (al-ashahh).
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
5
Understand the underlying principle
The wipe is a concession (rukhsah). When the foot is substantially wetted, the preventer (khuff) no longer justifies the concession; the original obligation (washing the foot) takes effect.
This explains why the wipe becomes invalid—the requirement (wajib) of washing the foot is revived.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فهم كلام الفحول كما دل على قصر باعه في علم الأصول .اهـ. قوله: (فقد علمت صحة ما بحثه المحقق الخ) قال في الشرنبلالية :قلت لكن لا يلزم من وجود فرع يخالف فرعاً غيره بطلانه، كيف وقد ذكره قاضيخان في فتاواه بقوله : ما مسح الخف إذا دخل الماء خفه وابتل من رجله قدر ثلاثة أصابع أو أقل لا يبطل . مسحه لأن هذا القدر لا يجزىء عن غسل الرجل فلا يبطل به حكم المسح ، وإن ابتل به جميع القدم وبلغ الكعب بطل المسح. مروي ذلك عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله اهـ. وذكره أيضاً في التتارخانية ثم قال : ويجب غسل الرجل الأخرى ذكره في حيرة الفقهاء. وعن الشيخ الفقيه أبي جعفر إذا أصاب الماء أكثر إحدى رجليه ينقض مسحه ويكون بمنزلة الغسل. وبه قال بعض المشايخ، وفي الذخيرة وهو الأصح وبعض مشايخنا قالوا لا ينتقض المسح على كل حال. وقال الزيلعي في نواقض المسح : وذكر المرغيناني أن غسل أكثر القدم ينقضه في الأصح اهـ. فهذا نص على صحة هذا الفرع وضعف ما يقابله اهـ كلامه قوله: (وتعقبه تلميذه الخ) قال في الشرنبلالية : أجاب شيخنا العلامة المحبي أدام الله تعالى نفعه عن هذا المنع بأن صحة الغسل داخل الخف الآن إنما هو باعتبار المانع فإذا زال المانع عمل المقتضى عمله لحصوله بعد الحدث في الحقيقة حال التخفيف، فإذا نزع وتمت المدة لا يجب الغسل لظهور عمل المقتضى الآن اهـ.
Understand the speech of the leading scholars as it indicates the limitation of his capacity in the science of principles. End. His statement: (You have known the correctness of what the muhaqqiq researched, etc.) He said in al-Shurnublaliyyah: I say, but it does not necessarily follow from the existence of a branch that contradicts another branch its invalidity. Indeed, Qadikhan mentioned it in his fatwas saying: Whoever wipes the khuff, if water enters his khuff and wets from his foot the amount of three fingers or less, it does not invalidate his wipe because this amount is not sufficient for washing the foot, so it does not invalidate the ruling of wiping. If it wets the entire foot and reaches the ankle, the wipe is invalid. That is narrated from Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him). End. He also mentioned it in al-Tatarkhaniyyah, then said: And it is obligatory to wash the other foot. Mentioned in Hiyarat al-Fuqaha. From al-Shaykh al-Faqih Abu Ja'far: If water hits most of one of his feet, it nullifies his wipe and is like washing. Some mashayikh said this. In al-Dhakhira, it is the most correct. Some of our mashayikh said: The wipe is not nullified in any case. Al-Zayla'i said in Nawaqid al-Mash: Al-Marghinani mentioned that washing most of the foot nullifies it in the most correct view. This is a text on the correctness of this branch and the weakness of its opposite. End of his speech. His statement: (And his student objected, etc.) He said in al-Shurnublaliyyah: Our teacher al-Allamah al-Muhibbi (may Allah perpetuate his benefit) answered this objection by saying that the correctness of washing inside the khuff now is only by consideration of the preventing factor. When the preventing factor is removed, the requirement acts, because it occurs after the minor event in reality during the state of convenience. So if he removes [the khuff] and the period ends, ghusl is not obligatory because the requirement's action has become evident now. End.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the effect of water entering the khuff on the validity of the wipe. Qadikhan reports from Abu Hanifa that if water enters the khuff and wets less than three fingers of the foot, the wipe remains valid because that amount is not sufficient to constitute a wash. If the entire foot becomes wet up to the ankle, the wipe is invalid. Some scholars, like Abu Ja'far, hold that if most of one foot becomes wet, the wipe is nullified. Others hold that the wipe is never nullified by water inside the khuff. The preferred view (as in al-Dhakhira and supported by al-Marghinani and al-Zayla'i) is that wetting most of the foot nullifies the wipe. The commentator then discusses an objection from a student and the answer that when the preventing factor (the khuff) is removed, the requirement of washing the foot becomes effective. This shows the nuance in Hanafi fiqh: the wipe is a concession, and if water effectively reaches the foot in a substantial way, the concession is no longer valid.

Key Terms
لمعة (lum'ah): A dry spot on the body after ghusl that was not washed.
نقض المسح (naqd al-mash): Nullification of the state of wiping, requiring the removal of khuffs and washing of feet.
المسح على الخفين (al-mash 'ala al-khuffayn): Wiping over leather socks (khuffs) as a substitute for washing the feet in wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view, what happens if water enters the khuff and wets most of the foot?
A) The wipe remains valid.
B) The wipe is invalid and the foot must be washed.
C) Only the part that got wet needs to be washed.
D) The khuff must be removed immediately.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the mufta bihi is that wetting most of the foot inside the khuff invalidates the wipe, requiring removal and washing of the feet.

Ruling on a Junub's Dry Spot and Wearing Khuffs
Clarifies a specific scenario of wiping over khuffs after a dry spot.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping over khuffs when a junub had a dry spot after ghusl, and apply the reasoning to a similar case.

Core Idea
A junub's dry spot does not permanently prevent wiping over khuffs once the spot is washed.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario: a junub person performs ghusl but misses a small dry spot on the body, then puts on khuffs, later washes that spot, and then has a minor hadath. The question arises: can he wipe over his khuffs? The Hanafi school, as reported in al-Khulasa and supported by al-Halabi, rules that he may. This teaching clarifies the reasoning and conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
List the sequence: (1) junub, (2) ghusl with a dry spot left, (3) wearing khuffs, (4) washing the spot, (5) having a minor hadath. Recognize that the key point is the timing of washing the spot relative to the hadath.
2
Recall the general rule for wiping over khuffs
Wiping is allowed only if the khuffs were worn after complete purification (ghusl or wudhu). Here, the person was still junub when wearing due to the dry spot.
3
Understand the removal of janabah
When the dry spot is washed, the janabah is fully removed retroactively for the purpose of future acts. So when the minor hadath occurs, the person is in a state of minor impurity, not major.
The text from al-Halabi states: 'the foot does not become junub again by seeing water'.
4
Apply the ruling
Since the minor hadath occurs after complete purification, the khuffs are treated as if they were worn after ghusl. Hence, wiping is permissible.
The ruling from al-Khulasa: 'he wipes'.
5
Note the scope
The ruling applies regardless of the size of the dry spot (lum'ah or more). The key is that the spot is washed before the minor hadath.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فإذا أحدث بعد ذلك إلى قوله لأنه عاد جنباً) قال العلامة الحلبي في شرح المنية ما ذكره ليس بسديد لأن الرجل بعد غسلها إذ ذاك لا تعود جنابتها برؤية الماء ولا يلزم غسلها مرة أخرى لأجل تلك الجنابة كما لو غسلهما أولاً ثم لبس الخف ثم أكمل الغسل وإنما حل بهما بعد الغسل حدث والمسح لأجل الحدث جائز. وصرح في الخلاصة أن الجنب إذا اغتسل وبقي على جسده لمعة فلبس الخف ثم غسل اللمعة ثم أحدث يمسح اهـ. ولا فرق بين بقاء لمعة أو أكثر في بقاء الجنابة وقد لبس الخف باقية ببقاء اللمعة وجوز له المسح ، فكذا يجوز في الصورة المذكورة فليتأمل.
His statement: (When he has a minor event after that until his statement: 'because he became junub') al-Allamah al-Halabi said in Sharh al-Munyah: What he mentioned is not correct because the foot after washing it at that time does not become junub again by seeing water, and it is not necessary to wash it again for that janabah, just as if he had washed them first, then wore the khuff, then completed the ghusl, and only a minor event occurred on them after the ghusl, and wiping for the minor event is permissible. And it is explicitly stated in al-Khulasa that if a junub performs ghusl and a dry spot remains on his body, then he wears the khuff, then washes the dry spot, then has a minor event, he wipes. End. And there is no difference between the remainder of a spot or more in the persistence of janabah, and he wore the khuff while it persisted by the spot, and he is allowed to wipe. So similarly, it is permissible in the mentioned scenario, so let one reflect.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_statement that addresses a question: what happens if a junub person performs ghusl but misses a spot (dry), wears khuffs, then later washes the dry spot, and then has a minor hadath? The text clarifies that the janabah remains due to the dry spot, but once the spot is washed, the person becomes pure. At that point, the khuffs were worn while the person was still junub (due to the spot), but the ruling from al-Khulasa is that he may wipe after the minor hadath because the janabah is considered as having been removed upon washing the spot, and the khuffs are now worn by a person who has completed ghusl. The key point is that the janabah does not retroactively affect the feet after the spot is washed; the wiping is permissible. This resolves a potential confusion where one might think the janabah continues even after washing the spot.

Key Terms
لمعة (lum'ah): A small area of skin left dry after ghusl.
جنب (junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.
خف (khuff): Leather sock that covers the feet and ankles, over which wiping is permitted in wudhu under certain conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He must remove the khuffs and wash his feet.
B) He may wipe over his khuffs.
C) He must repeat the ghusl.
D) He must perform wudhu without wiping.

Key Takeaway
Wiping over khuffs is permissible for a junub who washes a dry spot from ghusl before a minor hadath, because the janabah is removed upon washing the spot.

Menstruation and Khuff Wiping: The Hanafi Analogy to Janabah
Ruling on menstruation and nifas with khuff wiping, based on Abu Yusuf's principle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khuff wiping during menstruation and explain the qiyas to janabah based on Abu Yusuf's principle.

Core Idea
Menstruation prevents khuff wiping because it is legally analogous to janabah in requiring ghusl.

This lesson examines the application of khuff wiping rules to women experiencing menstruation or postpartum bleeding. The text from Sharh Munyat al-Musalli establishes that such states are treated like janabah, thus prohibiting the concession of wiping. We will explore the reasoning based on Abu Yusuf's principle and the condition that khuffs must be worn upon purification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key ruling
Find the explicit statement that wiping over khuffs during menstruation or nifas does not suffice for washing the feet.
Look for phrases like 'لا ينوب المسح على الخفين'.
2
Trace the basis: Abu Yusuf's principle
Note that the text explicitly says this ruling is based on Abu Yusuf's principle. Understand that Abu Yusuf considers the minimum menstruation as two days and two nights, making it akin to janabah.
Contrast with Abu Hanifa and Muhammad who may have different views.
3
Understand the legal analogy (qiyas)
See how menstruation is analogized to janabah: the khuff does not prevent transmission of impurity to the foot, just as in janabah.
The hadith of Safwan is cited as evidence for janabah.
4
Analyze the scenario conditions
The text details when a woman wears khuffs in a state of purification then menstruates, and when she wears them during menstruation. The key condition is that khuffs must be worn upon purification for wiping to be valid.
Focus on the phrase 'غسل الرجلين واجب لفوات شرط المسح'.
5
Note the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The difference in ruling: a menstruating woman with khuffs must wash her feet in wudu instead of wiping.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

وفي شرح منية المصلي : قوله من كل حدث موجب للوضوء احترازاً من الجنابة وما في معناها مما الغسل كالحيض على أصل أبي يوسف في حق المرأء إذا كانت مسافرة لأن أقل الحيض عنده يومان وليلتان وأكثر اليوم الثالث والنفاس فإنه لا ينوب المسح على الخفين في هذه الأحداث عن غسل الرجلين لعدم جعل الخف مانعاً من سرايتها إلى الرجل شرعاً كما صرح به في الجنابة حدث صفوان المتقدم، ويقاس الحيض والنفاس في ذلك عليها إن لم يكن فيهما إجماع اهـ . وإنما جعل الحيض مبنياً على أصل أبي يوسف لظهور أنه لا يتأتى على أصلهما فإنها إذا توضأت ولبست الخفين ثم أحدثت وتوضأت ) ومسحت ثم حاضت كان ابتداء المدة . من وقت الحدث، فإذا انقطع الدم لثلاثة أيام انتقض المسح قبلها فلا أن يتصور يمنع المسح لأجل غسل الحيض بمضي المدة. وإن لبستهما في الحيض فغسل الرجلين واجب لفوات شرط المسح وهو لبس الخفين على طهارة، والمقصود تصوير المسألة بحيث لا يكون مانع من مسح الخفين سوى وجوب الاغتسال وصوره عدم مسح ا النفساء أنها لبست على طهارة ثم نفست وانقطع قبل ثلاثة وهي مسافرة أو قبل يوم وليلة وهي مقيمة . لأنه امتنع لانتقاضه وهي اللمعة ثم أحدث يمسح اهـ. ولا فرق بين بقاء لمعة أو أكثر في بقاء الجنابة وقد لبس الخف باقية ببقاء اللمعة وجوز له المسح ، فكذا يجوز في الصورة المذكورة فليتأمل. قوله : (وروى إلا من جنابة قال بعض المحققين: تقرير هذا الاستثناء والاستدراك الحاصلين بـ«إلا» و«لكن هو أن الاستثناء من النزع لأنه أرخص لهم المسح مع ترك النزع ثم استثنى منه الجنابة فكأنه قال : لا تنزعوها إلا عند غسل الجنابة ثم قال مستدركاً لكن عن بول أو غائط أو نوم فلا تنزعوها، وبيان ذلك أن قوله إلا من جنابة تقديره أمرنا أن ننزعها من جنابة وهذه جملة إيجابية فلما أراد أن يستدرك جاء
And in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli: His statement: 'from every minor event that necessitates wudu' is an exception from janabah and what is similar to it of that which requires ghusl, like menstruation according to the principle of Abu Yusuf regarding women when she is traveling, because the minimum of menstruation according to him is two days and two nights, and the maximum is the third day, and post-childbirth bleeding. For wiping over khuffs does not suffice for washing the feet in these [states] due to the lack of making the khuff a preventer from its transmission to the foot legally, as was stated for janabah in the hadith of Safwan mentioned earlier. Menstruation and postpartum bleeding are analogized to it if there is no consensus on them. He made menstruation based on the principle of Abu Yusuf because it is clear that it is not possible on his principle [the other two?] because if she performs wudu and wears khuffs, then has a minor event and performs wudu and wipes, then menstruates, the beginning of the period is from the time of the minor event. If the blood stops after three days, the wipe is nullified before that, so it is not conceivable to prevent wiping due to the ghusl of menstruation by the passage of time. If she wears them during menstruation, then washing the feet is obligatory because the condition of wiping is missing, which is wearing khuffs upon purification. The purpose is to depict the case such that there is no preventer of wiping except the obligation of ghusl, and its picture is the absence of wiping for the postpartum woman that she wore upon purification then gave birth and the bleeding stopped before three [days] while she is traveling, or before a day and a night while she is resident. Because it is prevented due to its nullification. And it is the dry spot, then he had a minor event and he wipes. There is no difference between the remainder of a spot or more in the persistence of janabah, and he wore the khuff with the spot persisting, and he was allowed to wipe. So similarly, it is allowed in the mentioned scenario, so let one reflect. His statement: (And it was narrated 'except from janabah'.) Some muhaqqiqun said: The explanation of this exception and the istidrak (correction) achieved by 'illa' and 'lakin' is that the exception is from removal, because he granted them the concession of wiping while not removing, then he excepted from it janabah, as if he said: Do not remove them except at the time of washing for janabah. Then he said correcting: but from urine, feces, or sleep, so do not remove them. The explanation is that his saying 'except from janabah' is estimated as 'We were commanded to remove them for janabah' and this is a positive sentence. Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage discusses the application of khuff wiping rules to women in menstruation (hayd) and postpartum bleeding (nifas). The author cites Sharh Munyat al-Musalli, which states that the condition of 'from every minor event necessitating wudu' in the hadith excludes janabah and its analogues like menstruation. This is on the principle of Abu Yusuf, who considers that menstruation requires ghusl, and thus wiping over khuffs does not suffice for washing the feet during menstruation. The reasoning is that the khuff does not legally prevent the transmission of impurity from the foot during these states, just as in janabah. The text then explores the scenarios when a woman wears khuffs in a state of purification, then menstruates, and the duration of the wipe. It concludes that if she wears them during menstruation, she must wash her feet because the condition of wearing them on purification is lost. The postpartum woman is given as an example. The passage then transitions to the interpretation of the hadith's exception. The exception 'illa min janabah' is analyzed as a positive command to remove khuffs for janabah, and the istidrak (correction) with 'lakin' restores the concession for minor impurities. This shows the precision in Hanafi understanding of the hadith: the general permission to wipe is for minor impurities, and janabah is excluded, but the exclusion is from removal, meaning they must be removed for janabah. The text is slightly fragmented at the end.

Key Terms
حيض (hayd): Menstrual bleeding in women, which requires ghusl after cessation.
نفاس (nifas): Post-childbirth bleeding, treated similarly to hayd.
استثناء (istithna'): Exception in the hadith; 'illa' excludes a case from the general ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a menstruating woman wiping over her khuffs if she wore them before menstruation?
A) Wiping is valid as long as the khuffs were worn in purity.
B) Wiping is invalid, and she must wash her feet.
C) Wiping is valid only if she is a traveler.
D) She must remove the khuffs immediately.

Key Takeaway
Menstruation is analogous to janabah for khuff wiping, but the ruling depends on whether the khuffs were worn in a state of purity.

The Hadith Exception 'Except from Janabah': Hanafi Interpretation of Istithna' and Istidrak
Interpretation of the hadith's exception and istidrak.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi interpretation of the hadith exception 'illa min janabah' using the concepts of istithna' and istidrak.

Core Idea
The hadith's exception 'except from janabah' is a positive command to remove khuffs for janabah, while 'but' restores the concession for minor impurities.

This lesson focuses on the precise linguistic analysis of the prophetic hadith regarding khuff wiping. The text presents a muhaqqiq's explanation of the exception (istithna') and the subsequent correction (istidrak) using 'illa' and 'lakin'. Understanding this demonstrates Hanafi precision in usul and fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith phrasing and its parts
The hadith includes a general permission to wipe, an exception 'illa min janabah', and a corrective statement with 'lakin'.
The exception is from removal (naz'), not from wiping.
2
Understand the role of 'illa' (except) as istithna'
The phrase 'except from janabah' is interpreted as a positive command: 'We were commanded to remove them for janabah.' This is an implicit positive jumla.
The exception here is mufaragh (empty) – it excludes janabah from the general permission.
3
Analyze the istidrak (correction) with 'lakin' (but)
After the exception, the hadith says 'but from urine, feces, or sleep, do not remove them.' This is an istidrak to re-include minor impurities under the concession.
The 'lakin' restores the ruling for minor hadath.
4
Reconstruct the full meaning
The hadith effectively means: 'Do not remove khuffs except for janabah, but for minor impurities, do not remove them.' This clarifies that the concession is for minor impurities only.
This is the Hanafi understanding of the hadith's structure.
5
Note the legal implication
Wiping is valid for minor hadath only; janabah and its analogues (like menstruation) require removal and washing of feet.
This supports the earlier ruling on menstruation.
