Duration of Wiping over Khuff and Its Start Time
Stating the duration and its starting point

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the duration of wiping over khuff for a resident and a traveler, and explain why the Hanafi school counts the period from the first hadath after wearing rather than from the first wipe or from the time of wearing.

Core Idea
The wiping period over khuff starts when the barrier is needed — from the first impurity after wearing.

This lesson examines the ruling on the duration of wiping over khuff and the juristic disagreement about when the period begins. The Hanafi school, following the majority of scholars, holds that the clock starts from the moment the first ritual impurity (hadath) occurs after donning the khuff, not from the first wipe or from the act of wearing. Understanding the rationale—that the khuff is a legal barrier against impurity—clarifies why the starting point matters and how to apply the duration in practice.

Guided Path
1
State the duration ruling
Identify the basic ruling: a resident may wipe for one day and one night; a traveler for three days and three nights. This is from the source commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq.
The duration is fixed by sunnah and agreed upon by the majority of scholars.
2
Identify the dispute on starting point
Three views exist: (1) from the first hadath after wearing (Hanafi and majority), (2) from the first wiping (Ahmad in one narration, al-Nawawi), (3) from the time of wearing (al-Hasan al-Basri, al-Subki). The Hanafi view is mufta bihi.
The dispute is about the occasion that triggers the beginning of the period.
3
Understand the Hanafi proof
The hadiths indicate that the khuff is a legal barrier (mani') preventing the spread of hadath to the foot. Therefore, the period is counted from the moment the barrier is needed, which is when hadath occurs.
This is a dalil naqli supported by multiple explicit hadiths.
4
Apply the rule: the bandage case
The text from al-Muhit provides a test case: if one wears khuff, then wipes over a bandage, then the wound heals after a hadath, the duration is completed from the original hadath because the wearing was upon a complete purification (the bandage wiping substitutes for washing).
This illustrates that the starting point is consistently the first hadath after wearing, preserving the condition of complete purity at the time of wearing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (يوماً وليلة للمقيمم وللمسافر (ثلاثاً) هذا بيان لمدة المسح أي صح المسح يوماً وليلة الخ. وهذا قول جمهور العلماء أصحابنا والشافعي وأحمد والحجة لهم أحاديث كثيرة صريحة يطول سردها وقد اختلف القول عن مالك في جوازه للمقيم ومشى أبو زيد في رسالته على جوازه للمقيم. قوله من وقت الحدث بيان لأول وقته ولا يعتبر من وقت المسح الأول كما هو رواية عن أحمد واختاره جماعة منهم النووي وقال لأنه مقتضى أحاديث الباب الصحيحة، ولا من وقت اللبس كما هو محكي عن الحسن البصرى واختاره السبكي من متأخري الشافعية لأنه وقت جوازه الرخصة والحجة للجمهور أن أحاديث الباب كلها دالة على أن الخف جعل مانعاً من سراية الحدث إلى الرجل شرعاً فتعتبر المدة من وقت المنع لأن ما (وفي المحيط وإن لبس الخف ثم مسح على الجبيرة ثم برىء يكمل مدته) أي برىء بعد ما أحدث فإنه يكمل مدة المسح على الخف لأنه إذا توضأ بعد هذا الحدث ثم برىء صار محدثاً بالحدث السابق والحدث السابق متأخر عن اللبس فيكون اللبس على طهارة كاملة بخلاف المسألة الآتية، وكذا السابقة فإن الحدث الذي ظهر كان قبل اللبس فلا يكون لبس على طهارة كاملة فيجب نزع الخف. وانظر ما المسألة بأن المسح بعد اللبس قوله : فتعتبر المدة من وقت المنع) قال الرملي : هذا فائدته تصویر
His saying: 'A day and a night for the resident and for the traveler three' – this is an explanation of the duration of wiping, i.e., wiping is valid for a day and a night, etc. This is the statement of the majority of scholars: our companions, al-Shafi'i, and Ahmad. Their evidence is many explicit hadiths that would be lengthy to list. A statement was differed regarding Malik concerning its permissibility for the resident, and Abu Zayd in his Risala followed the permissibility for the resident. His saying: 'from the time of hadath' is an explanation of its beginning. It is not considered from the time of the first wiping, as is a narration from Ahmad and chosen by a group including al-Nawawi, who said it is the requirement of the authentic hadiths of the chapter. Nor from the time of wearing, as is reported from al-Hasan al-Basri and chosen by al-Subki among the later Shafi'is, because it is the time the license becomes permissible. The proof for the majority is that all the hadiths of the chapter indicate that the khuff is made a legal barrier preventing the spread of hadath to the foot, so the period is counted from the time of prevention. Because what (in al-Muhit: 'If he wore the khuff then wiped over the bandage, then it healed, he completes his period') – i.e., it healed after he had hadath, then he completes the period of wiping over the khuff because when he performed wudu after this hadath then it healed, he becomes hadath by the previous hadath, and the previous hadath is subsequent to the wearing, so the wearing was upon complete purification, unlike the following case, and likewise the previous, for the hadath that appeared was before the wearing, so there was no wearing upon complete purification, so it is necessary to remove the khuff. And look at the case that the wiping is after wearing – his saying: 'the period is considered from the time of prevention' – al-Ramli said: this is its benefit for depiction.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof commentary on the duration of wiping over khuff. The base text (from Kanz al-Daqa'iq) states: 'A day and a night for the resident, and for the traveler three [days]'. The commentator, Ibn Nujaym, explains that this is the duration during which wiping is valid. He notes that this is the position of the majority of scholars including the Hanafis, Shafi'is, and Ahmad ibn Hanbal. There is a difference reported from Malik regarding its permissibility for the resident, and Abu Zayd (a Hanafi scholar) followed the permissibility for the resident in his Risala. The key point of legal dispute is the starting point of this duration. The correct Hanafi position (and the majority view) is that the duration begins from the time of the first hadath (ritual impurity) that occurs after wearing the khuff, not from the time of the first wiping, nor from the time of wearing. This is because the khuff acts as a legal barrier (mani') preventing the spread of hadath to the feet; thus, the count starts when the barrier becomes active, which is at the moment of hadath. The proof is that the hadiths of the chapter indicate this. In contrast, a narration from Ahmad and al-Nawawi holds that it starts from the first wiping. Al-Hasan al-Basri and al-Subki consider it from the time of wearing. The Hanafi argument for the majority view is that the hadiths show that the khuff is a barrier, so the duration is counted from when the barrier is needed (i.e., after hadath). The passage also includes an application from al-Muhit: if one wears khuff, then wipes over a bandage (jabira) and later the wound heals, the duration is completed from the original hadath because the later hadath occurred after a complete purification (since the bandage wiping is like washing). This reinforces that the starting point is the first hadath after wearing, and that the condition of complete purification must be met at that time.

Key Terms
مدة المسح (muddāt al-masḥ): The time limit for which wiping over khuff is valid: one day and night for a resident, three days and nights for a traveler.
وقت الحدث (waqt al-ḥadath): The moment when the first ritual impurity occurs after wearing the khuff; this marks the start of the permissible wiping period.
الخف مانع (al-khuff māni‘): The khuff is considered a legal barrier that prevents the spread of hadath to the feet, so wiping is a substitute for washing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, from which point does the permissible wiping period over khuff begin for a resident?
A) From the moment he first wipes over the khuff.
B) From the time he wore the khuff.
C) From the time of the first hadath (ritual impurity) that occurs after wearing.
D) From the time of the first prayer he performs after wearing.

Key Takeaway
The duration of wiping over khuff is fixed by sunnah, and the clock starts from the first hadath after wearing, not from the wipe or the wearing time.

Wiping over Khuffs Combined with Bandages
Explains rulings when wiping over bandages before wearing khuffs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid khuff-wiping after bandage-wiping and apply the ruling to cases of healed and unhealed wounds.

Core Idea
Bandage-wiping substitutes for washing only temporarily; if the wound heals, the substitute lapses and the khuff-wipe becomes invalid.

This passage from al-Bada'i' and al-Muhit addresses a practical ambiguity: what happens when a person has a bandage on the foot, wipes over it in wudu, then wears khuffs, and later the wound heals? The Hanafi school applies the principle that wiping over a bandage is analogous to washing the skin underneath, but that analogy holds only while the bandage is needed. Once the wound heals, the original impurity re-emerges, breaking the chain of purity required for khuff-wiping. Understanding this ruling requires careful attention to the timing of events.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key act and its prerequisite
The act is wearing khuffs after bandage-wiping. The prerequisite is that the feet must be in a state of complete ritual purity (taharah kamilah) at the time of wearing.
2
Recognize the legal fiction of bandage-wiping
Bandage-wiping (masah ala al-jabirah) is legally treated as washing the underlying skin, so it establishes complete purity for that foot.
This is a rukhsa (concession) for the injured.
3
Apply to the combined scenario
If bandage-wiping occurs before wearing khuffs, the khuffs are worn upon complete purity, making subsequent wiping on khuffs valid.
4
Distinguish based on healing
If the wound heals, the bandage is no longer needed, so the bandage-wiping no longer serves as a substitute. The original impurity becomes effective again, retroactively breaking the purity at the time of wearing khuffs. Hence, wiping on khuffs becomes invalid.
The khuffs must be removed for the next wudu.
5
Examine additional scenarios from al-Muhit
Healing alters the obligation to wash the healed part. If healing occurs after an event, the khuff-wiping duration continues. If healing occurs without an event, washing the spot restores purity, allowing subsequent khuff-wiping. If an event occurs before washing after healing, the khuff must be removed.
The order of events is critical.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي البدائع لو توضأ ومسح على جبائر قدميه ولبس خفيه أو كانت إحدى رجليه صحيحة فغسلها ومسح على جبائر الأخرى ولبس خفيه ثم أحدث، فإن لم يكن بريء الجرح مسح على الخفين لأن المسح على الجبائر كالغسل لما تحته فحصل لبس الخفين على طهارة كاملة كما لو أدخلهما مغسولتين حقيقة في الخف، وإن كان بريء الجرح نزع خفيه لأنه صار محدثاً بالحدث السابق فظهر أن اللبس حصل لا على طهارة. وفي المحيط: وإن لبس الخف ثم مسح على الجبيرة ثم برىء يكمل مدته لأنه لزمه غسل ما برىء بحدث متأخر عن اللبس، وإن لم يحدث حتى برىء فغسل موضعه ثم أحدث فله أن يمسح على خفيه لأنه لما غسل ذلك الموضع فقد كملت الطهارة فيكون الحدث طارئاً على طهارة كاملة، وإن أحدث قبل أن يغسل موضع الجراحة بعد البرء لا يمسح بل ينزع الخف لأن الحدث طرأ على طهارة ناقصة.
In al-Bada'i': If he performed wudu and wiped over bandages on his feet and put on his khuffs, or if one foot was healthy so he washed it and wiped over bandages on the other and put on his khuffs, then he had an event: if the wound had not healed, he wipes over the khuffs because wiping over bandages is like washing what is under them, so putting on the khuffs occurred upon complete purity as if he had inserted them truly washed into the khuff. If the wound had healed, he removes his khuffs because he became impure by the previous event, so it becomes evident that the wearing did not occur upon purity. In al-Muhit: If he wore the khuff then wiped over the bandage, then healed, he completes his duration because washing the healed part became obligatory due to an event after the wearing. If he did not have an event until he healed, then washed the place, then had an event, then he may wipe over his khuffs because when he washed that spot, purity became complete, thus the event occurs upon complete purity. If he had an event before washing the wounded spot after healing, he does not wipe but removes the khuff because the event occurred upon incomplete purity.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage from al-Bada'i' and al-Muhit addresses a complex scenario where a person combines wiping over bandages (jabirah) with wearing khuffs. The key principle is that for khuff-wiping to be valid, the khuffs must be put on while in a state of complete taharah. If one has bandages on the foot, wiping over the bandages counts as washing the underlying skin for the purpose of achieving taharah. Thus, if one wipes over bandages and then wears khuffs, the khuffs are deemed to have been worn upon complete purity, similar to having washed the feet normally. However, if the wound heals later, the earlier taharah is retroactively broken because the bandage-wiping was only a substitute for washing, so the original impurity from before the bandage reappears. Consequently, the khuffs must be removed. Al-Muhit adds details about the sequence: if the healing occurs after an event, the khuff-wiping duration continues because the healing imposes a new washing obligation that is separate. If healing occurs without an event, washing the spot completes the purity, and subsequent events allow wiping. But if an event occurs before the spot is washed after healing, the khuff must be removed because the event happened while purity was incomplete.

Key Terms
جبيرة (jabīrah): A bandage or splint applied to a wound or fracture.
طهارة كاملة (ṭahārah kāmilah): Complete purity; the state of being free from both major and minor hadath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person wipes over a bandage on his foot, wears khuffs, then the wound heals before he has any event, what is the ruling?
A) He continues wiping on khuffs normally.
B) He must remove the khuffs and cannot wipe on them.
C) He may wipe only if he washes the healed spot first.
D) He may wipe but only for the remaining duration.

Key Takeaway
Bandage-wiping provides complete purity for khuff-wearing only while the wound is unhealed; upon healing, the purity must be restored by washing the healed spot before any hadath occurs.

8 min
Duration of Khuff Wiping and Its Start Time
Defines duration and clarifies the ruling's commencement from hadath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the duration of wiping over khuffs and identify the correct starting point (hadath) by evaluating the proofs from the majority's hadith and the reasoning of al-Sarakhsi.

Core Idea
Duration of wiping starts at the first hadath, not at wearing or wiping—because the khuff becomes a barrier only after impurity strikes.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq defines the time limit for wiping over khuffs and clarifies the disputed beginning of that period. The majority of scholars agree on the duration (one day/night for resident, three for traveler), but they differ on when the clock starts. The Hanafi school, along with the majority, holds that it begins at the first hadath after wearing. We will examine the proofs and the practical consequence (thamarat al-khilaf) of this difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
What is the duration and start time according to the Hanafi school?
Duration: 1 day/night resident, 3 traveler; start at hadath.
2
Identify opposing views
What are the alternative start times (from wiping, from wearing) and who holds them?
From wiping: al-Nawawi; from wearing: al-Subki.
3
Follow the majority's proof
How do the hadith support the start at hadath?
Hadith show khuff prevents transmission of hadath, so duration from moment of prevention.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
How does al-Sarakhsi rebut the other views?
From wearing would force removal without hadath; from wiping allows indefinite postponement.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference in the example given?
End times vary by start point: hadath, wiping, or wearing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (يوماً وليلة للمقيم وللمسافر ثلاثاً) هذا بيان لمدة المسح أي يمسح يوماً وليلة الخ. وهذا قول جمهور العلماء أصحابنا والشافعي وأحمد والحجة لهم أحاديث كثيرة صريحة يطول سردها وقد اختلف القول عن مالك في جوازه للمقيم ومشى أبو زيد في رسالته على جوازه للمقيم. قوله من وقت الحدث بيان لأول وقته ولا يعتبر من وقت المسح الأول كما هو رواية عن أحمد واختاره جماعة منهم النووي وقال لأنه مقتضى أحاديث الباب الصحيحة، ولا من وقت اللبس كما هو محكي عن الحسن البصري واختاره السبكي من متأخري الشافعية لأنه وقت جواز الرخصة والحجة للجمهور أن أحاديث الباب كلها دالة على أن الخف جعل مانعاً من سراية الحدث إلى الرجل شرعاً فتعتبر المدة من وقت المنع. وفي المبسوط لشمس الأئمة السرخسي: وابتداؤها عقيب الحدث لأنه لا يمكن اعتبار المدة من وقت اللبس فإنه لو لم يحدث بعد اللبس حتى يمر يوم وليلة لا يجب عليه نزع الخف ولا يمكن اعتباره من وقت المسح لأنه لو أحدث ولم يمسح ولم يصل أياماً لا إشكال أنه يمسح بعد ذلك فكان العدل في الاعتبار من وقت الحدث. وثمرة الخلاف تظهر فيمن توضأ بعدما انفجر الصبح ولبس خفيه وصلى الفجر ثم أحدث بعد طلوع الشمس ثم توضأ ومسح على خفيه بعد زوال الشمس؛ فعلى قول الجمهور يمسح إلى ما بعد طلوع الشمس من اليوم الثاني إن كان مقيماً ومن اليوم الرابع إن كان مسافراً، وعلى قول من اعتبر من وقت المسح يمسح إلى ما بعد الزوال من اليوم الثاني إن كان مقيماً ومن اليوم الرابع إن كان مسافراً، وعلى قول من اعتبر من وقت اللبس يمسح إلى ما بعد طلوع الفجر من اليوم الثاني إن كان مقيماً ومن اليوم الرابع إن كان مسافراً. وفي معراج الدراية معزياً إلى المجتبى والمقيم في مدة مسحه قد لا يتمكن إلا من أربع صلوات وقتية بالمسح كمن توضأ ولبس خفيه قبل الفجر ثم طلع الفجر وصلاها وقعد قدر التشهد فأحدث لا يمكنه أن يصلي من الغد على هيئة الأولى لاعتراض ظهور الحدث في آخر صلاته، وقد يصلي خمساً وقد يصلي ستاً كمن أخر الظهر إلى آخر الوقت ثم أحدث وتوضأ ومسح وصلى الظهر في آخر وقته ثم صلى الظهر من الغد وقد يصلي به على هذا الوجه سبعاً على الاختلاف.
His statement (a day and a night for the resident and for the traveler three): This is an explanation of the duration of wiping: i.e., he wipes a day and a night, etc. This is the statement of the majority of scholars—our fellows, al-Shafi'i, and Ahmad. Their proof is many clear hadith whose enumeration would be lengthy. Malik's statement differed regarding its permissibility for the resident, and Abu Zayd in his treatise went with its permissibility for the resident. His statement (from the time of the event) is an explanation of its beginning time. It is not considered from the time of the first wiping, as is a narration from Ahmad, chosen by a group including al-Nawawi, who said it is required by the authentic hadith of the chapter. Nor from the time of wearing, as is reported from al-Hasan al-Basri and chosen by al-Subki among later Shafi'is, because it is the time of permissibility of the dispensation. The proof for the majority is that all the hadith of the chapter indicate that the khuff is made a legal barrier preventing the transmission of the event to the foot, so the duration is considered from the time of prevention. In al-Mabsut of Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi: Its beginning is immediately after the event because it is not possible to consider the duration from the time of wearing, for if he does not have an event after wearing until a day and night pass, he is not obligated to remove the khuff. Nor is it possible to consider it from the time of wiping, because if he has an event and does not wipe or pray for days, there is no doubt that he wipes after that. So the fair consideration is from the time of the event. The practical difference appears in the case of one who performed wudu after dawn had broken and put on his khuffs, prayed Fajr, then had an event after sunrise, then performed wudu and wiped over his khuffs after noon. According to the majority, he wipes until after sunrise of the second day if resident and the fourth day if traveler. According to the one who considers from the time of wiping, he wipes until after noon of the second day if resident and the fourth day if traveler. According to the one who considers from the time of wearing, he wipes until after dawn of the second day if resident and the fourth day if traveler. In Mi'raj al-Dirayah attributed to al-Mujtaba: The resident in his wiping duration may not be able to perform more than four time-bound prayers with wiping, like one who performed wudu and put on his khuffs before dawn, then dawn broke and he prayed it, and sat for the amount of tashahhud, then had an event—he cannot pray the next day in the first manner due to the occurrence of the event at the end of his prayer. And he may pray five, and may pray six, like one who delayed Zuhr to the end of its time, then had an event, performed wudu and wiped, prayed Zuhr at the end of its time, then prayed Zuhr the next day. And he may pray with this manner seven, according to difference.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the duration for wiping over khuffs: one day and night for a resident, three days for a traveler. The majority of scholars (including Hanafis, Shafi'is, and Hanbalis) hold this position, supported by authentic hadith. The point of dispute is when the duration begins. The correct view (and the majority view) is that it begins from the time of the first hadath (impurity event) after wearing the khuffs, not from the time of first wiping nor from the time of wearing. Al-Sarakhsi in al-Mabsut provides the reasoning: if it started from wearing, a person who never has an event would be required to remove the khuffs after a day, which is not the case. If it started from wiping, a person who delays wiping for days could still wipe after a long time, which is illogical. Therefore, the count begins when the khuff's preventive function actually takes effect, which is at the event. A practical difference (thamar al-khilaf) is illustrated with a detailed example involving times of day and different starting points. The passage also notes that a resident may manage only four obligatory prayers within the duration, but under certain conditions may pray up to seven.

Key Terms
مدة المسح (muddatu al-masḥ): The time limit for which wiping over khuffs remains valid.
ثمرة الخلاف (thamarat al-khilāf): The practical consequence arising from differing legal opinions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does the wiping duration begin after wearing khuffs?
A) At the time of putting on khuffs
B) At the first hadath after wearing
C) At the first wiping
D) At the next prayer time

Key Takeaway
The duration for wiping over khuffs (1 day/night for resident, 3 for traveler) begins at the first hadath after wearing, not at wearing or wiping.

The Obligatory Area for Wiping Over the Khuff
Defines the precise area of the khuff to be wiped

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligatory area for wiping over the khuff and apply the ruling to determine the validity of common wiping errors.

Core Idea
Only the upper part of the khuff from toes to shin must be wiped; inner and sides are not permissible.

When performing wudu while wearing khuffs, it is essential to wipe the correct area. The Hanafi school specifies that only the upper part (zahir) of the khuff is obligatory, covering from the toes to the start of the shin. This lesson clarifies the exact area and addresses a minor intra-madhhab difference on whether wiping the inner part is recommended.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act
Wiping over khuffs is a substitute for washing feet in wudu. The act itself is wajib.
2
Locate the Obligatory Area
The passage states the area is the upper part (zahir) from toes to shin, as specified in al-Mubtagha.
The phrase 'from the tips of the toes to the bound of the shin' defines the exact zone.
3
Understand Prohibitions
Wiping the inner, heel, sides, or ankles is not permissible (la yajuz). Doing so does not fulfill the wiping obligation.
4
Analyse the Intra-Hanafi Variant
Al-Muhit says combining inner is not sunnah; al-Bada'i' says it is mustahabb (recommended) unless there is impurity on the inner part. The latter is the practiced view.
This difference affects only the recommended practice, not the obligatory requirement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (على ظاهرهما مرة) بيان لمحل المسح حتى لا يجوز مسح باطنه أو عقبه أو ساقيه أو جوانبه أو كعبه. وفي المبتغى بالغين المعجمة وظهر القدم من رؤوس الأصابع إلى معقد الساق صريح في أن المدة تعتبر من أول وقت الحدث لا من آخره. قوله : (وفي غيره نفي الاستحباب) أي في غير المحيط نفي استحباب مسح باطن مع ظاهره وهو المراد من قول المحيط ولا يسن. لكن في النهر عن البدائع: يستحب عندنا الجمع بين الظاهر والباطن في المسح إلا إذا كان على باطنه نجاسة.
His statement (on their uppers once) is an explanation of the place of wiping, such that it is not permissible to wipe its inside, its heel, its sides, or its ankles. In al-Mubtagha (with ghayn mu'jama) and the back of the foot from the tips of the toes to the bound of the shin, it is explicit that the duration is considered from the beginning of the time of the event, not from its end. His statement: (And in other than it, negation of recommendation) meaning in other than al-Muhit, the recommendation of wiping the inside along with the outside is negated, and that is what is meant by the statement of al-Muhit: and it is not sunnah. But in al-Nahr from al-Bada'i': It is recommended with us to combine between the outer and inner in wiping unless there is impurity on the inner part.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage specifies the location for wiping over khuffs: only the upper part (zahir) of the khuff is to be wiped. It is not permissible to wipe the inner part (batin), the heel, the sides, or the ankle. The source al-Mubtagha explicitly mentions 'the back of the foot from the tips of the toes to the bound of the shin' (i.e., the instep area). The passage also addresses a minor difference: while al-Muhit states that wiping both the outer and inner is not sunnah, al-Bada'i' (cited in al-Nahr) holds that it is recommended (mustahabb) to combine both, unless there is najasah on the inner part. This falls within the realm of recommended acts, not obligatory.

Key Terms
ظاهر الخف (ẓāhir al-khuff): The upper part of the khuff that covers the foot's upper side from toes to shin.
باطن الخف (bāṭin al-khuff): The inner lining or the part of the khuff that touches the sole of the foot.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Wiping over khuffs requires wiping only the upper part from toes to shin; wiping any other area does not fulfill the obligation.

Determining the Start of the Wiping Period Over Khuffs
Determining the start of the wiping period and its practical consequence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on when the wiping period for khuffs begins, explain the rational proof (dalil aqli) for this view, and apply the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) to calculate the end of the period in a given scenario.

Core Idea
The wiping period begins not from wearing or wiping, but from the first hadath after wearing.

Many assume the clock for wiping over khuffs starts ticking the moment you pull them on, but the Hanafi school establishes a different trigger: the first occurrence of hadath (minor impurity) after wearing. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq unpacks the rational proof behind that position and shows why it matters in practice through a concrete scenario. Understanding the start point is crucial for determining when the period ends and when you must remove the khuffs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Recognize that the act in question is wiping over khuffs (mash ala al-khuffayn). The ruling is permissibility (mubah) within a limited period. The key issue is when that period begins.
2
Locate the dalil (proof) for the Hanafi start point
The passage quotes al-Sarakhsi from al-Mabsut, presenting a rational argument (dalil aqli). It eliminates the alternative starting points (wearing and wiping) as impractical or illogical, leaving hadath as the only consistent point.
This is a classic example of istidlal bi al-‘aql – reasoning to determine the proper legal cause (sabab) for the period.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof establishes the ruling)
The proof shows: (a) if the period started from wearing, then a person who never has hadath would never need to remove the khuffs – but that contradicts the purpose of the period; (b) if it started from wiping, then a person who delays wiping indefinitely would have an endless period – also illogical. Therefore, the period must be tied to the hadath, which is the actual cause for needing wudu.
This is a qiyas or istihsan reasoning: the 'illa (effective cause) is the hadath itself.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (differing views)
The passage identifies three opinions: (1) majority (Hanafi) – from hadath; (2) from the time of wiping; (3) from the time of wearing. The thamarah (practical consequence) is then illustrated with a detailed scenario.
The dispute is primarily within the Hanafi school or between Hanafi and other schools? The passage says 'جمهور' (majority) but does not name the others. In Hanafi texts, these alternatives are often attributed to Abu Yusuf or others.
5
Evaluate the tarjih and apply the thamarah
The passage strongly supports the hadath view, calling it the 'just consideration'. The thamarah scenario shows how the end point of the period shifts depending on which start point is chosen. For a resident who has hadath after sunrise on day 1 and wipes after noon, the end point varies from sunset of day 1 to sunrise of day 2.
The scenario is crucial: it shows that the same set of actions leads to different obligations under different rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يوهم مسح قبل ذلك طهارة الغسل ولا تقدير فيها، فإذن التقدير في التحقيق إنما هو لمدة منعه شرعاً وإن كان ظاهر اللفظ التقدير للمسح أو اللبس والخف إنما منع من وقت الحدث. وفي المبسوط لشمس الأئمة السرخسي : وابتداؤها عقيب الحدث لأنه لا يمكن اعتبار المدة من وقت اللبس فإنه لو لم يحدث بعد اللبس حتى يمر يوم وليلة لا يجب عليه نزع الخف ولا يمكن اعتباره من وقت المسح لأنه لو أحدث ولم يمسح ولم يصل أياماً لا إشكال أنه لا بعد ذلك فكان يمسح العدل في الاعتبار من وقت الحدث .اهـ. وكذا في النهاية ومعراج الدراية معزياً إلى مبسوط شيخ الإسلام. فاستفيد منه أن مضي المدة رافع لجواز المسح أعم من كونه مسح أو لا، فالأولى أن لا يجعل مضي المدة ناقضاً للمسح لأنه أنه إذا لم يكن هناك فلا أثر لمضيها كما لا يخفى. وثمرة الخلاف تظهر فيمن توضأ بعدما انفجر الصبح ولبس خفيه وصلى الفجر ثم أحدث بعد طلوع الشمس ثم توضأ ومسح على خفيه بعد زوال الشمس؛ فعلى قول الجمهور يمسح إلى ما بعد طلوع الشمس من اليوم الثاني إن كان مقيماً ومن اليوم الرابع إن كان مسافراً، وعلى قول من اعتبر من وقت المسح يمسح إلى ما بعد الزوال من اليوم الثاني إن كان مقيماً . ومن اليوم الرابع إن كان مسافراً، وعلى قول من اعتبر من وقت اللبس يمسح إلى ما بعد طلوع الفجر من اليوم الثاني إن كان مقيماً ومن اليوم الرابع إن كان مسافراً. وفي معراج الدراية معزياً إلى المجتبى والمقيم في مدة مسحه قد لا يتمكن إلا من أربع صلوات وقتية بالمسح كمن توضأ ولبس خفيه قبل الفجر ثم طلع الفجر وصلاها وقعد قدر التشهد فأحدث لا يمكنه أن يصلي من الغد على هيئة الأولى لاعتراض ظهور الحدث في آخر صلاته، وقد يصلي خمساً وقد يصلي ستاً كمن أخر الظهر إلى آخر الوقت ثم أحدث وتوضأ ومسح وصلى الظهر في آخر وقته ثم صلى الظهر من الغد وقد يصلي به على هذا الوجه سبعاً على الاختلاف . اهـ .
It [the text] suggests wiping before that is the purification of ghusl and there is no estimation in it. So the estimation in reality is only for the duration of its legal prohibition, even if the apparent wording is estimation for the wiping or wearing, and the khuff is only prohibited from the time of hadath. In al-Mabsut of Shams al-A'immah al-Sarakhsi: Its beginning is immediately after hadath, because it is impossible to consider the duration from the time of wearing, for if he does not have hadath after wearing until a day and night pass, he is not obliged to remove the khuff; and it is impossible to consider it from the time of wiping, because if he has hadath and does not wipe nor pray for days, there is no doubt that there is no [effect] after that, so the just consideration is from the time of hadath. End. Similarly in al-Nihayah and Mi'raj al-Dirayah, citing the Mabsut of Shaykh al-Islam. From this it is understood that the passing of the period removes the permissibility of wiping, regardless of whether he wiped or not. So it is better not to make the passing of the period a naqid of wiping, because if there is no [wiping], then the passing has no effect, as is not hidden. The fruit of the disagreement appears in one who performed wudu after dawn, wore his khuffs, prayed Fajr, then had hadath after sunrise, then performed wudu and wiped over his khuffs after noon. According to the majority, he may wipe until after sunrise of the second day if a resident, and until the fourth day if a traveler. According to the one who considers from the time of wiping, he may wipe until after noon of the second day if a resident, and until the fourth day if a traveler. According to the one who considers from the time of wearing, he may wipe until after dawn of the second day if a resident, and until the fourth day if a traveler. In Mi'raj al-Dirayah citing al-Mujtaba: The resident in his wiping period may not be able to perform except four obligatory prayers by wiping, like one who performed wudu and wore his khuffs before Fajr, then dawn appeared and he prayed it, and sat for the amount of tashahhud, then had hadath, he cannot pray the next day in the same manner due to the intervention of hadath at the end of his prayer. And he may pray five, and may pray six, like one who delayed Zuhr to the end of its time, then had hadath, performed wudu and wiped and prayed Zuhr at the end of its time, then prayed Zuhr the next day. And he may pray seven in this manner, according to the disagreement. End.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq discusses a key point: from when does the period for wiping over khuffs begin? The text clarifies that the estimation (taqdir) is not for the wiping itself or the wearing, but for the duration of the legal prohibition (i.e., the time during which one is allowed to wipe). The Hanafi position, as stated by al-Sarakhsi in al-Mabsut, is that the period begins immediately after the first hadath (impurity) that occurs after wearing the khuffs. This is because considering the time of wearing is impractical (one might not have hadath for a day), and considering the time of wiping is also impractical (one might delay wiping). Therefore, the period is measured from the hadath. The commentary then draws a practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf): following different opinions about the start time leads to different endings of the period in a specific scenario. The majority (Hanafi) view is that the period ends after sunrise of the next day for a resident (traveler: fourth day). Other views (from time of wiping or wearing) give different endings. The passage also notes that a resident might only be able to perform four prayers with one wipe if hadath occurs at a certain time, but could pray up to seven depending on the scenario.

Key Terms
الخف (al-khuff): A leather sock that can be wiped over in place of washing the feet in wudu.
الحدث (al-hadath): Minor impurity (such as passing wind, urine, etc.) that necessitates wudu.
المدة (al-mudda): The legally prescribed period for wiping: one day and night for a resident, three days for a traveler.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) From the time of wearing the khuff
B) From the first hadath after wearing
C) From the time of the first wipe
D) From sunrise

Key Takeaway
The wiping period for khuffs begins at the first hadath after wearing, not at wearing or wiping, a position based on rational proof that avoids logical contradictions and yields a clear practical rule.

The Place of Wiping Over Khuffs: Top Only or Both?
Establishing the place of wiping and refuting the Shafi'i view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the place of wiping over khuffs, explain the Hanafi dalil from the hadith of Ali, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument from the hadith of al-Mughira.

Core Idea
Only the top of the khuff is wiped – the Hanafi school rejects qiyas when text is present.

In this lesson, we examine a key point of ikhtilaf between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the place of mash over khuffs. The Hanafi school, based on a clear hadith from Ali (RA), limits wiping to the apparent upper surface (al-dahir), while the Shafi'i school, relying on a different narration, recommends wiping both top and bottom. We will analyze the evidence and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what exactly the Hanafi school holds regarding the place of wiping on the khuff. Is it only the top, or also the bottom and sides?
The passage explicitly states that wiping is limited to the apparent (dahir) of the khuff, and that wiping the inner sole, heel, sides, etc., is not permitted.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and their evidence
What is the Shafi'i view, and what hadith do they cite as proof? The Shafi'i school recommends wiping both top and bottom, and they rely on the hadith of al-Mughira.
The hadith from al-Mughira is narrated by Abu Dawud.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
How does the Hanafi school rebut the Shafi'i proof? The Hanafis argue that the hadith of al-Mughira is weak (weakened by al-Tirmidhi and Abu Dawud). If it were authentic, they interpret it as referring to the parts near the ankle and toes, not the sole. They also emphasize that the hadith of Ali (RA) explicitly negates qiyas in favor of direct observation.
The Hanafi response also includes a discussion of why qiyas (which would suggest wiping the bottom) is rejected in favor of the revealed text (tawqif).
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference between the two positions? For the Hanafis, wiping only the top suffices; for the Shafi'is, wiping the top is fard and wiping the bottom is sunnah.
This difference affects the validity of the mash in practice.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Why is the Hanafi position considered stronger according to the author? The Hanafi evidence is based on an authentic hadith of Ali (RA), while the Shafi'i evidence is considered weak in transmission.
The author (al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah) and later commentators uphold the Hanafi view as mufta bihi.

المعراج أن الاستحباب قول لبعض مشايخنا أيضاً قوله : فمعناه ما يلي الساق الخ) أي المراد
His saying (on their apparent face once) is an explanation of the place of wiping, so that it is not permissible to wipe its inner sole, or its heel, or its legs, or its sides, or its ankle. In al-Mubtagha (with the dotted ghayn) and the top of the foot from the tips of the toes to the ankle of the khuff. The strap. End. And in al-Muhit: It is not sunnah to wipe the inner sole of the khuff with its apparent, contrary to al-Shafi'i, because the sunnah was legislated to complete the obligations, and completion is only realized in the place of the obligation, not elsewhere. End. And in others, negation of recommendation (istihbab), and that is intended. Al-Shafi'i argued with the hadith of al-Mughira ibn Shu'bah who said: I performed wudu for the Messenger of Allah in the Battle of Tabuk, and he wiped the top of the khuff and its bottom. Narrated by Abu Dawud. And for us [Hanafis] is what Abu Dawud and al-Bayhaqi narrated through multiple chains from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him): 'If religion were by opinion, the bottom of the khuff would be more deserving of wiping than its top, but I saw the Messenger of Allah wiping over the apparent of his khuffs.' He meant that the foundations of sharia were not established through qiyas, but their way is tawqif (revelation), and it is not permissible to use qiyas to reject tawqif. And qiyas would require that the inner sole be more deserving of wiping because it meets the ground with its mud, dust, and filth, while the top does not meet it, but he did not use qiyas because he saw the Messenger of Allah wiping the apparent of the khuff without its inner sole. This indicates that his intent was to negate qiyas in the presence of text. This is what al-Jassas mentioned in his Usul. End. Similarly in Ghayat al-Bayan. This indicates, as apparent from al-Nihayah and others, that by 'inner' they mean the place of treading, not what contacts the skin. And the muhaqqiq in Fath al-Qadir objected that by this estimation the priority of wiping the inner sole if by opinion does not appear, but the immediate understanding of Ali's saying is that which contacts the skin, because the obligatory part of washing the foot in wudu is not to remove khabath but hadath, and the place of treading on the inner sole of the foot is like its apparent. Similarly, what was narrated from Ali with the wording 'the bottom of the khuff is more deserving than its top for wiping' must be understood that 'bottom' means the side that contacts the skin, because it is lower than the upper side facing the sky as we mentioned. End. And what was narrated that he wiped its top and bottom was weakened by al-Tirmidhi and Abu Dawud and others, and if [authentic], its meaning is what is adjacent to the leg and what is adjacent to the toes, to reconcile between it and the hadith of Ali. This is in Ghayat al-Bayan. And it was objected that it is befitting to permit wiping the bottom and heel because it is a substitute for washing, so it is permissible in all the place of washing, like wiping the head, for it is permitted on all of the head even though he (peace be upon him) is reported to have wiped the forelock. The answer: his action here is originally not rationally comprehensible, so all that is transmitted of the law regarding the action and the place is considered, unlike his wiping on the forelock, which is an explanation of what is established by the Book, not an institution of law, so action must be according to what achieves the explanation, which is the amount, because the place is known by text, so there is no need to make his action an explanation for it. And it was further objected that wiping should be obligatory up to the leg in observance of all what was transmitted. And similarly in Sharh al-Hidayah of al-Ayni citing al-Badai', but what I saw in my copy of al-Badai' attributes it to al-Shafi'i, for he said: It is reported from al-Shafi'i that if he confines to the inner sole it is not permissible, and the recommended according to him is to combine, etc. And this is what I saw in al-Tatar-Khaniyyah where he said: The place of wiping is the apparent of the khuff, not its inner sole. And al-Shafi'i said: Wiping the apparent of the khuff is fard, and on its inner sole it is sunnah, and the better according to him is to place his right hand on the apparent of the khuff and his left hand on the inner sole and wipe both on his entire foot. End. The pronoun 'according to him' refers to al-Shafi'i, as is not hidden. Yes, it is mentioned in al-Mi'raj that recommendation is also a saying of some of our shaykhs. His saying: 'so its meaning is what is adjacent to the leg, etc.' that is the intended meaning.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage addresses the place of wiping over khuffs, a point of difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. The Hanafi position, clearly stated, is that only the apparent (dahir) of the khuff — i.e., the upper surface — is to be wiped. Wiping the inner sole (batin), heel, sides, or ankle is not permitted. The school does not even consider it sunnah to wipe the inner sole, contrary to the Shafi'i view. The main evidence for the Hanafi school is the hadith of Ali (RA): 'If religion were by opinion, the bottom would be more deserving... but I saw the Messenger of Allah wiping over the apparent of his khuffs.' This hadith explicitly negates qiyas in favor of direct observation. The Shafi'i school relies on the hadith of al-Mughira that the Prophet wiped both top and bottom, but the Hanafi response is that this hadith is weak (weakened by al-Tirmidhi and Abu Dawud). If accepted, they interpret it as referring to the part near the ankle and toes, not the sole. The commentary also addresses a potential qiyas: since wiping is a substitute for washing, why not wipe the entire area? The answer is that the Prophet's action defines the place, unlike the head where wiping is established by the Qur'an and the Prophet's wiping of the forelock is explanatory. Thus, the Hanafi school confines wiping to the apparent top.

Key Terms
الظاهر (al-dahir): The apparent top surface of the khuff, which is the only place wiped according to the Hanafi school.
الباطن (al-batin): The inner sole of the khuff; also interpreted as the part contacting the skin or the place of treading.
المسح (al-mash): Wiping with wet hands over the khuff in place of washing the feet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school discussed in the passage, what part of the khuff is wiped?
A) The top (dahir) only
B) The inner sole (batin) only
C) Both top and bottom
D) The heel only

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school limits wiping over khuffs to the top surface only, based on the authentic hadith of Ali (RA) that rejects qiyas in favor of the Prophet's explicit action.

Ruling on Wiping Only the Outer Surface of the Khuff
Dispute with Shafi'i on whether the inner sole of the khuff should be wiped

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that wiping the inner sole of the khuff is not sunnah, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Only the outer surface of the khuff is wiped; the inner sole is not recommended, as the sunnah completes the obligation, and obligation is on the outer part.

This passage presents a key point of ikhtilaf between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools on the details of wiping the khuff during wudu. While the obligation is to wipe the outer surface, the question is whether the inner sole (batin) should also be wiped as sunnah. The Hanafi school, relying on a hadith of 'Ali (ra) and the principle that sunnah complements only the place of obligation, holds that it is not sunnah. The Shafi'i school, citing a hadith of al-Mughirah, views it as sunnah. This lesson unpacks the arguments and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Position
Identify the exact ruling: it is not sunnah nor mustahab to wipe the inner part of the khuff. Only the outer part is wiped. Note the ruling level: makruh tanzih.
2
Identify the Opponent and their View
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that wiping the inner part is sunnah (mustahab). Some narrations suggest it may be obligatory. Recognize the basis of ikhtilaf.
3
Follow the Opponent's Proof
Examine the hadith of al-Mughirah (ra) which states the Prophet wiped both the upper and lower parts of the khuff. Understand the chain and its evaluation by hadith critics.
The hadith is narrated by Abu Dawud but declared weak by al-Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud, and others.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Response
The Hanafis present the hadith of 'Ali (ra) which explicitly negates qiyas in the presence of text. The Prophet wiped only the outer surface, so qiyas is overruled. Also, the Shafi'i hadith is weak; if authentic, it is interpreted differently (wiping near the leg and toes, not the entire sole).
The Hanafis also argue that sunnah completes the obligation, and the obligation is on the outer part only.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Practical consequence: In Hanafi practice, one should not wipe the inner sole; doing so is makruh tanzih. In Shafi'i practice, it is sunnah to wipe both, preferably with a single motion covering the outer part first then the inner part.
The mufta bihi in Hanafi school is the negation of istihbab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة - باب المسح على الخفين
الشراك اهـ. وفي المحيط ولا يسن مسح باطن الخف مع ظاهره خلافاً للشافعي لأن السنة شرعت مكملة للفرائض والإكمال إنما يتحقق في محل الفرض لا في غيره اهـ. وفي غيره نفي الاستحباب وهو المراد واحتج الشافعي بحديث المغيرة بن شعبة قال: وضأت رسول الله الله في غزوة تبوك فمسح أعلى الخف وأسفله. رواه أبو داود. ولنا ما رواه أبو داود والبيهقي من طرق عن علي رضي الله عنه : لو كان الدين بالرأي لكان أسفل الخف أولى بالمسح من أعلاه، وقد رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يمسح على ظاهر خفيه. أراد أن أصول الشريعة لم تثبت من طريق القياس وإنما طريقها التوقيف وغير جائز استعمال القياس في رد التوقيف وكان القياس أن يكون باطن الخف أولى بالمسح لأنه يلاقي الأرض بما عليها من طين وتراب وقذر ولا يلاقيها ظاهره إلا أنه لم يستعمل القياس لأنه رأى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يمسح ظاهر الخف دون باطنه، وهذا يدل على أن مراده كان نفي القياس مع النص. كذا ذكره الجصاصي في أصوله اهـ. كذا في غاية البيان. وهذا يفيد كظاهر ما في النهاية وغيرها أن المراد بالباطن عندهم محل الوطء لا ما يلاقي البشرة وتعقبهم المحقق في فتح القدير بأنه بتقديره لا تظهر أولوية مسح باطنه لو كان بالرأي بل المتبادر من قول علي رضي الله عنه ذلك ما يلاقي البشرة، وهذا لأن الواجب من غسل الرجل في الوضوء ليس لإزالة الخبث بل الحدث ومحل الوطء من باطن الرجل فيه كظاهره وكذا ما روي عن علي فيه بلفظ «لكان أسفل الخف أولى أعلاه بالمسح من يجب أن يراد بالأسفل الوجه الذي يلاقي البشرة لأنه أسفل من الوجه الأعلى المحاذي للسماء كما ذكرنا اهـ. وما روي أنه مسح أعلاه وأسفله فقد ضعفه الترمذي وأبو داود وغيرهما، ولو فمعناه ما صح يلي الساق وما يلي الأصابع توفيقاً بينه وبين حديث علي. كذا في غاية البيان
Book of Purification - Chapter on Wiping over Khuffs: The strap... etc. In al-Muhit: It is not sunnah to wipe the inner part of the khuff along with its outer part, contrary to al-Shafi'i, because the sunnah was legislated to complete the obligations, and completion is only realized in the place of the obligation, not elsewhere. In another [source] it is a negation of recommendation (istihbab), which is the intended meaning. Al-Shafi'i argued with the hadith of al-Mughirah ibn Shu'bah who said: I performed wudu for the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) in the expedition of Tabuk, and he wiped the upper part of the khuff and its lower part. Narrated by Abu Dawud. Our evidence is what Abu Dawud and al-Bayhaqi narrated through multiple chains from 'Ali (ﷺ): 'If religion were by opinion, the lower part of the khuff would be more deserving of wiping than its upper part; and I saw the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) wiping on the outer surface of his khuffs.' He meant that the principles of the Shari'ah are not established through analogy (qiyas); rather their path is based on revelation (tawqif), and it is not permissible to use analogy to reject revelation. By analogy, the inner part of the khuff would be more deserving of wiping because it meets the ground with its dirt, dust, and filth, whereas the outer part does not meet it. But he did not use analogy because he saw the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) wiping the outer surface of the khuff without its inner part. This indicates that his intent was to negate analogy in the presence of the text. Thus al-Jassas mentioned it in his Usul. End quote. Thus in Ghayat al-Bayan. This indicates, as appears from al-Nihayah and others, that what is meant by 'inner' (al-batin) according to them is the place of treading (mahl al-wat') not what touches the skin. The scholar in Fath al-Qadir objected to them that with this interpretation, the superiority of wiping its inner part if it were by opinion would not be apparent; rather, the immediate understanding from 'Ali's statement is what touches the skin, because the obligatory washing of the foot in wudu is not for removing filth (khabath) but for [removing] impurity (hadath), and the place of treading on the inner part of the foot is like its outer part. Similarly, what was narrated from 'Ali with the wording: 'The lower part of the khuff would be more deserving of wiping than its upper part' should be interpreted that by 'lower' is meant the side that touches the skin because it is lower than the upper side facing the sky as we mentioned. End quote. As for what was narrated that he wiped its upper and lower part, al-Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud, and others declared it weak. If [it were authentic], then its meaning would be what is adjacent to the leg and what is adjacent to the toes, as a reconciliation between it and the hadith of 'Ali. Thus in Ghayat al-Bayan.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the ruling of wiping the inner part (batin) of the khuff during wudu. The passage begins by stating the Hanafi ruling: it is not sunnah to wipe the inner part of the khuff along with the outer part. In fact, it is not even mustahab (recommended). The reason given is that the sunnah complements the obligation (fard), and the place of obligation for wiping is the outer surface of the khuff, which replaces the washing of the feet. Therefore, completing the obligation applies only to the place of the obligation, not elsewhere. Al-Shafi'i argues using the hadith of al-Mughirah that the Prophet wiped both the upper (a'la) and lower (asfal) parts of the khuff. The Hanafi response is based on the hadith of 'Ali (ra) which states that if religion were by opinion (qiyas), the lower part would be more deserving of wiping, but the Prophet wiped only the outer surface. This demonstrates that qiyas cannot override a clear text. The Hanafis also argue that by qiyas, the inner part (which touches the ground) would be more deserving of wiping because it gets dirtier, but the Prophet's practice overrides this. The passage then discusses the meaning of 'inner' (batin) and 'upper/lower' (a'la/asfal). Some scholars interpret 'inner' as the part that touches the skin, but the preferred Hanafi view is that it refers to the sole of the foot (the part that treads). The hadith reporting wiping both upper and lower is declared weak by hadith critics, and if authentic, it would be interpreted as wiping from the leg to the toes in a single motion (not the entire sole). This lesson is a clear example of Hanafi reliance on textual evidence (tawqif) over qiyas when a text exists.

Key Terms
مسح (mash): The act of wiping a wet hand over a khuff or other body part as a substitute for washing.
خف (khuff): A leather sock or boot that covers the feet and ankles, worn for walking.
باطن الخف (batin al-khuff): The inner part of the khuff that touches the foot (the part facing the skin).
ظاهر الخف (zahir al-khuff): The outer surface of the khuff (the side facing outward).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on wiping the inner part (batin) of the khuff during wudu?
A) It is sunnah mu'akkadah.
B) It is mustahab (recommended).
C) It is not sunnah nor mustahab; it is makruh tanzih.
D) It is wajib.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches that only the outer surface of the khuff is wiped; the inner part is not sunnah, based on the hadith of 'Ali and the principle that sunnah completes the obligation at its place.

The Minimum Wipe Over Khuffs: Three Fingers Required
Discussion on the minimal amount of the khuff to be wiped and the number of fingers required.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum amount of the khuff wipe required by the Hanafi school and apply the hadith proofs to justify the three-finger ruling.

Core Idea
Three fingers suffice for wiping the khuff; extending to the leg is sunnah, not fard.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses a key issue in wudu: the minimum amount of wiping over leather khuffs. The Hanafi school, drawing on explicit hadith and linguistic principles, establishes that wiping just the front part with three fingers is sufficient. This lesson walks through the proofs and the scholarly objections, clarifying what is obligatory and what is recommended.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Determine the disputed point: the extent of the required wipe over khuffs—does it cover the entire foot, reach the leg, or just the front part?
The passage objects that wiping the lower part and heel should be allowed by qiyas with head wiping.
2
Examine the qiyas objection and response
Analyze the objection that wiping the entire foot is analogous to wiping the head, and the Hanafi response distinguishing the head case as an explanation of the Quran, not a new legislation.
The response asserts that the Prophet's head wipe was an explanation of the verse, so it indicates the minimum, not the whole head.
3
Analyze the hadith evidence for three fingers
Look at the two hadiths: the Prophet wiping lines with his fingers and his statement to the man. Understand how the plural 'fingers' (asabi') minimally indicates three, and how the interrogative 'أما يكفيك' establishes sufficiency.
The hadiths are the primary dalil for the three-finger ruling.
4
Distinguish between obligatory and sunnah components
Identify that the basic wipe is fard/wajib, the extension to the leg (madd) is sunnah, and showing lines is sunnah but not required for validity.
The passage reconciles different narrations by making the basic wipe obligatory and the extension sunnah.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Conclude that wiping the outer surface with at least three fingers in a single pass is sufficient; fewer fingers or wiping the inner side invalidates the wipe.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأورد أنه ينبغي جواز مسح الأسفل والعقب لأنه خلف عن الغسل فيجوز في جميع محل الغسل كمسح الرأس فإنه يجوز في جميع الرأس وإن ثبت مسحه عليه السلام على الناصية. وأجيب بأن فعله هنا ابتداء غير معقول فيعتبر جميع ما ورد به الشرع من رعاية الفعل والمحل بخلاف مسحه على الناصية فإنه بيان ما ثبت بالكتاب لا نصب الشرع فيجب العمل بقدر ما يحصل به البيان وهو المقدار لأن المحل معلوم بالنص فلا حاجة إلى جعل فعله بياناً له. وتعقب بأنه ينبغي أن يجب المسح إلى الساق رعاية لجميع ما ورد به الشرع فينبغي أن لا يجوز قدر ثلاث أصابع إلا بنص ولم يجب عنه في فتح القدير. وبأنه ينبغي أنه لو بدأ من الساق لا يجوز لما ذكرنا . فأجاب عن الثاني في فتح القدير بأنه لا يجب ما ورد به في محل الابتداء أو الانتهاء للعلم بأن المقصود إيقاع البلة على ذلك المحل. وأجاب عن الأول في معراج الدراية بأنه روي أنه عليه السلام مسح على خفيه من غير ذكر مد إلى الساق كما روي المد فجعل المفروض أصل المسح والمد سنة جمعاً . وتعقب بأنه ينبغي حمل المطلق على المقيد هنا لورودهما في حكم واحد في محل واحد كما في كفارة اليمين وأجيب بأن الروايتين لا يتساويان في الشهرة بل المطلق هو المشهور دون المقيد، ولئن سلمنا تساويهما لا يجب الحمل أيضاً لإمكان الجمع فإن مسحه عليه السلام لم يقتصر على مرة واحدة فلا يكون الإطلاق والتقييد في حكم واحد في حادثة واحدة بل في متعدد في نفسه فيثبت أصل المسح وسنية المد، وتعقب بأنه ينبغي أن يستحب الجمع بين مسح الظاهر والباطن لكونهما مرويين والجمع ممكن، فيثبت فرضية أصل المسح وسنية المسح على الظاهر والباطن. وأجيب بأن في إحدى الروايتين احتمالاً كما قدمناه فلا تثبت السنية بالشك، وقد يقال كان ينبغي على هذا أن يكون في صوم الكفارة مطلق الصوم واجباً والتتابع سنة ويكون هذا جمعاً بين القراءتين، ولهذا والله أعلم لم يرتض المحقق في فتح القدير بما أجاب به في معراج الدراية وفي البدائع ما يصلح جواباً عما في فتح القدير فإنه استدل على فرضية ثلاث أصابع بحديث علي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام مسح على ظهر خفيه خطوطاً بالأصابع قال : وهذا خرج مخرج التفسير للمسح. والأصابع اسم جمع وأقل الجمع الصحيح ثلاثة فكان هذا تقديراً للمسح بثلاث أصابع اليد اهـ. وهكذا ذكر الأقطع واستدل المصنف في المستصفى بأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم رأى رجلاً يغسل خفيه فقال : أما يكفيك مسح ثلاثة أصابع اهـ وهذا صريح في المقصود. وفي قوله مرة» إشارة إلى أنه لا يسن تكراره كمسح الرأس عملاً بما ورد أنه عليه السلام مسح ظاهر خفيه خطوطاً بالأصابع بطريق الإشارة إذ الخطوط إنما تكون إذا مسح مرة. كذا في المستصفى. ولم يذكر المصنف الخطوط للإشارة إلى الرد على ما يفهم من عبارة الطحاوي أنها كما هو ظاهر المجتبى فإنه ذكر أن إظهار الخطوط في المسح ليس بشرط في ظاهر الرواية ثم قال : وقال الطحاوي المسح على الخفين خطوطاً بالأصابع اهـ. والظاهر ظاهر الرواية، نعم إظهار الخطوط شرط السنية . قوله (بثلاث أصابع بيان لمقدار آلة المسح بطريق المنطوق ولبيان قدر الممسوح بطريق فكأنه قيل مسح من أسفله إلى أعلى ساقه .
It was objected that wiping the lower part and the heel should be permissible, because it is a substitute for washing, so it should be permissible over the entire place of washing, like wiping the head, for it is permissible over the entire head even though the Prophet (ﷺ) wiped over the forelock. The answer was that his action here (wiping over the forelock) is an initial action that is rationally understood (ghayr ma'qul), so all that is reported by the Shari'ah must be considered in terms of action and place. This is different from wiping over the forelock, because that is an explanation of what is established by the Book, not a legislation of a new act; so one must act according to what achieves the explanation, which is the amount, because the place is known by the text, so there is no need to make his action an explanation for it. It was objected that wiping to the leg should be obligatory, considering all that is reported by the Shari'ah, so the amount of three fingers should not be permissible except by text, and he did not answer that in Fath al-Qadir. Also, it should be that if one starts from the leg, it is not permissible, for what we mentioned. He answered the second in Fath al-Qadir by saying that what is reported regarding the beginning or ending place is not obligatory, because it is known that the purpose is to apply moisture to that place. He answered the first in Mi'raj al-Dirayah by saying that it is narrated that he (ﷺ) wiped over his khuffs without mentioning extension to the leg, just as extension is narrated, so he made the obligatory act the basic wipe and the extension (madd) as sunnah, as a reconciliation. It was objected that the absolute (mutlaq) should be restricted by the restricted (muqayyad) here because they both come in one ruling in one place, as in the expiation for an oath. The answer is that the two narrations are not equal in fame; rather, the absolute is more famous than the restricted. If we concede their equality, restriction is still not obligatory because reconciliation is possible. His (ﷺ) wiping was not confined to one occasion, so the absolute and restricted are not in one ruling in one single incident, but in multiple incidents. Thus, the basic wipe is established and the extension is sunnah. It was objected that combining wiping the outer and inner should be mustahab because both are narrated and combining is possible. Thus, the basic wipe would be fard, and wiping the outer and inner would be sunnah. The answer is that one of the two narrations has a possibility [of weakness], as we mentioned, so sunnah is not established by doubt. It may be said that according to this, in the expiation of fasting, absolute fasting would be wajib and consecutiveness would be sunnah, and this would be a reconciliation between the two recitations. For this reason, and Allah knows best, the investigator in Fath al-Qadir did not approve of what was answered in Mi'raj al-Dirayah. In al-Bada'i there is something that serves as an answer to what is in Fath al-Qadir, for it argued the obligatory nature of three fingers with the hadith of 'Ali (ra) that he (ﷺ) wiped on the back of his khuffs with lines by his fingers. He said: This came as an explanation (tafsir) of the wiping. The word 'fingers' is a plural noun (ism jam'), and the minimum of the sound plural is three. So this was a determinate of wiping by three fingers of the hand. End quote. Similarly, al-Aqta' mentioned and the author in al-Mustasfa argued with the hadith that the Prophet (ﷺ) saw a man washing his khuffs and said: 'Is it not sufficient for you to wipe three fingers?' End quote. This is explicit in the intended meaning. In the word 'once' (marrah) is an indication that repetition is not sunnah, like wiping the head, acting upon what was narrated: that he (ﷺ) wiped the back of his khuffs with lines by his fingers as a gesture, because lines only occur when one wipes once. Thus in al-Mustasfa. The author did not mention the lines to indicate a refutation of what is understood from the expression of al-Tahawi, as is apparent from al-Mujtaba, for he mentioned that showing lines in wiping is not a condition in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah). Then he said: And al-Tahawi said: 'Wiping over khuffs with lines by the fingers.' End quote. The apparent is the apparent narration. Yes, showing lines is a condition for sunnah. His statement: 'with three fingers' is an explanation of the amount of the instrument of wiping by way of explicit statement (mantuq) and to explain the amount of the wiped area by way of indication (dalalah). So it is as if it is said: 'He wiped from its lower part to the top of his leg.'
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof lesson on the extent of wiping over khuffs. It begins with an objection that wiping the lower part and heel should be permissible because wiping is a substitute for washing the foot, so it could cover the entire foot, like wiping the head (which can cover the whole head even though the Prophet wiped over the forelock). The answer distinguishes: wiping the forelock was an explanation of the verse on tayammum, not a new legislation, so it indicates the minimum, not the entire head. For khuffs, the place is known by text, so the Prophet's action is the standard. Then the discussion turns to whether the wipe must reach the leg (saaq). Some argue that since the Shari'ah reports both absolute and extended wipes, the minimal obligatory wipe is the basic wipe (giving moisture to the front part) and the extension (to the leg) is sunnah. This is supported by the hadith where the Prophet wiped lines on his khuffs with fingers, which implies using three fingers, and a separate hadith where the Prophet told a man that wiping three fingers is sufficient. The minimum of the plural 'fingers' is three, so three fingers are required. The wipe should be done once (not repeated), as lines indicate a single pass. The passage also addresses whether the inner part should be wiped, but reaffirms that only the outer is required. The relied-upon ruling is that the obligatory wipe is on the outer surface of the khuff with three fingers, without needing to reach the leg or cover the entire foot.

Key Terms
ثلاث أصابع (thalath asabi'): The minimum number of fingers required to wipe the khuff, derived from the hadith of three lines and the Prophet's statement.
المد (al-madd): The extension of the wipe from the toes to the leg (ankle area)
الأسفل والعقب (al-asfal wa al-'aqab): The lower part of the foot (sole) and the heel.
خطوط (khutut): Lines on the khuff made by the fingers during wiping, indicating a single pass.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum number of fingers required for wiping over khuffs according to the Hanafi school?
A) One finger
B) Two fingers
C) Three fingers
D) The whole hand

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires that wiping over khuffs be done with a minimum of three fingers on the outer surface, based on the hadith and linguistic interpretation; extension to the leg is sunnah.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
The Obligatory Measure of Wipe on Khuffs is Three Fingers
Determining the obligatory measure of wiping over khuffs as three fingers, with proofs and intra-Hanafi discussion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the obligatory measure of wiping over khuffs, cite the primary evidence (hadith), and identify the relied-upon position within the madhhab.

Core Idea
Three fingers from the hand — not the foot — is the obligatory measure for wiping khuffs, established by Sunnah and agreed upon by the later relied-upon position.

Determining the exact measure of wiping over khuffs (masah 'ala al-khuffayn) is essential for the validity of wudu. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling that the obligatory minimum is three fingers from the hand, based on explicit prophetic practice and the linguistic principle of plurals. We will examine the primary proofs, the intra-Hanafi discussion regarding which fingers count, and how this ruling is applied in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is wiping over khuffs during wudu. According to the Hanafi school, it is wajib (obligatory) to wipe with a minimum of three fingers from the hand. The term 'fard' used in the text means wajib in this context.
The ruling is for the substitute of washing the feet.
2
Locate the dalil
Two key hadith are cited: 1) The hadith of 'Ali that the Prophet (ﷺ) wiped over his khuffs making lines with his fingers. 2) The Prophet (ﷺ) told a man washing his khuffs, 'Is it not sufficient for you to wipe three fingers?'
Both hadith are ahad, thus zanni al-thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The word 'fingers' (asabi') is a sound plural indicating a minimum of three. The explicit statement 'three fingers' directly establishes the measure. The action of making lines implies a single wipe, so repetition is not required.
This reasoning uses Arabic grammatical rules for the minimum plural.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some Hanafis, like al-Karkhi, held that the three fingers are from the foot (toes). Others restricted it to the smallest fingers of the hand. The majority, including Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, maintained that it is three fingers from the hand generally.
The hand is the tool of wiping, so the measurement is by the tool, not the object.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the later books (fatawa mutakhkhirin) is that the obligatory wipe is with three fingers from the hand, and this is the view adopted by the majority of Hanafi scholars.
This ruling is consistent across most Hanafi fatwa works.

The Book of Purification - Chapter on Wiping over Khuffs
Considering all of the Shari'a, it should not be permissible [to wipe] the measure of three fingers except by text, and there is no obligation concerning it in Fath al-Qadir. And [it is said] that if he began from the leg it would not be permissible for what we mentioned. He answered the second in Fath al-Qadir: that it is not obligatory, what was reported about the beginning or the ending because it is known that the purpose is to place moisture on that place. And he answered the first in Mi'raj al-Dirayah: that it is narrated that he (peace be upon him) wiped over his khuffs without mentioning extending to the leg, just as extension was narrated, so the obligatory was made the original wipe and extension is sunnah as a combination. It was objected that the absolute should be carried to the restricted here because they both occur in one ruling in one place, as in the expiation of an oath. And it was answered that the two narrations are not equal in fame; rather, the absolute is the famous one without the restricted. And if we concede their equality, carrying is not obligatory either due to the possibility of combination, for his (peace be upon him) wiping was not limited to one time, so the absolute and restricted are not in one ruling in one incident but in multiple incidents in themselves, so the original wipe is established and the extension is sunnah. And it was objected that one should combine wiping the top and bottom because both are narrated and combination is possible, so the obligation of the original wipe and the sunnah of wiping the top and bottom would be established. And it was answered that in one of the two narrations there is a possibility as we mentioned, so sunnah is not established by doubt. And it may be said that according to this, in the fast of expiation, absolute fasting would be obligatory and consecutive fasting would be sunnah, and this would be a combination between the two readings. For this reason, perhaps, the investigator in Fath al-Qadir did not approve of what was answered in Mi'raj al-Dirayah, and in al-Bada'i' there is something that serves as an answer to what is in Fath al-Qadir, for he argued for the obligation of three fingers by the hadith of 'Ali that he (peace be upon him) wiped on the top of his khuffs with lines with the fingers. He said: This came as an explanation of wiping. And 'fingers' is a plural noun and the minimum of a sound plural is three, so this was an estimation of wiping with three fingers of the hand. End quote. And al-Aqta' mentioned likewise, and the author in al-Mustasfa argued that the Prophet (peace be upon him) saw a man washing his khuffs and said: 'Is it not sufficient for you to wipe three fingers?' End quote. This is explicit for the intended meaning. And in his saying 'once' is an indication that its repetition is not sunnah like wiping the head, acting on what is reported that he (peace be upon him) wiped the top of his khuffs with lines with the fingers by way of indication, for lines only occur when wiped once. Thus in al-Mustasfa. And the author did not mention the lines to indicate a refutation of what is understood from the expression of al-Tahawi, which is as apparent in al-Mujtaba, for he mentioned that showing lines in wiping is not a condition in the apparent narration, then he said: And al-Tahawi said: Wiping over khuffs with lines with fingers. End quote. And the apparent is the apparent narration. Yes, showing lines is a condition for sunnah.
Obligatory on
His saying (with three fingers) is an explanation of the measure of the tool of wiping by way of explicit statement, and to explain the measure of the wiped surface by way of
In the hadith, 'its upper part' means what is raised from it, i.e., from the side of the leg, and 'its lower part' means what is below it from the side of the toes, as if it was said: he wiped from its lower part to the upper part of his leg.
